981: ## 6. Permissions / RLS checklist
983: Three new tenant-scoped tables. Each MUST have the four requirements from `docs/spec-authoring-checklist.md § 4` (RLS policy, manifest entry, route guard, principal-scoped context).
989: | **RLS policy** | Included in migration `0327_create_operator_runs.sql`. Standard org+subaccount scoping via the existing `current_setting('app.organisation_id')` and `current_setting('app.subaccount_id')` GUCs. `FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` enabled (defeats owner-bypass). Pattern matches `agent_runs` and `iee_runs`. |
990: | **Manifest entry** | Added to `server/config/rlsProtectedTables.ts` in the same migration. `{ tableName: 'operator_runs', schemaFile: 'operatorRuns.ts', policyMigration: '0327_create_operator_runs.sql', rationale: 'Chain-link state for operator-managed backend; one row per chain link; tenant-scoped by org+subaccount.' }`. |
991: | **Route guard** | Reads go through `GET /api/operator-sessions/:operatorRunId/progress` — guards: `authenticate`, `requirePermission('AGENT_RUN_READ')`, and `setOrgGUC()` before the query. Direct-DB-access prohibition is enforced by `verify-rls-contract-compliance.sh`. |
994: ### 6.2 `operator_task_profiles`
998: | **RLS policy** | Included in migration `0328_create_operator_task_profiles.sql`. Same shape as `operator_runs`. |
999: | **Manifest entry** | Added to `rlsProtectedTables.ts` in the same migration. Rationale: "Persistent browser-profile metadata per operator task; tenant-scoped." |
1000: | **Route guard** | The fresh-profile-restart route (`POST /api/operator-tasks/:agentRunId/fresh-profile-restart`) guards: `authenticate`, `requirePermission('AGENT_RUN_ADMIN')` (org-admin equivalent for this action), `setOrgGUC()`. The debug-retention-extend route reuses the same guard set. |
1001: | **Principal-scoped context** | Profile-volume mount runs inside the adapter principal context. The GC job runs under a maintenance principal (existing `withAdminConnection` pattern for cron-like jobs) — see § 7. |
1003: ### 6.3 `subaccount_operator_settings`
1007: | **RLS policy** | Included in migration `0329_create_subaccount_operator_settings.sql`. Org+subaccount scoping. |
1008: | **Manifest entry** | Added to `rlsProtectedTables.ts` in the same migration. Rationale: "Per-subaccount operator runtime caps; tenant-scoped; org_admin write, manager read." |
1009: | **Route guard** | `GET /api/subaccounts/:subaccountId/operator-settings` → `authenticate`, `requirePermission('SUBACCOUNT_READ')`, `resolveSubaccount`, `setOrgGUC()`. `PATCH` → `authenticate`, `requirePermission('SUBACCOUNT_OPERATOR_SETTINGS_WRITE')`, `resolveSubaccount`, `setOrgGUC()`. The PATCH permission key is new in this spec — added to the permissions registry and the org-admin role's default grant. |
1014: - **`agent_runs`** — already RLS-protected; this spec only extends the `status` enum and does not change RLS policy.
1015: - **`llm_requests`** (or canonical cost-ledger table) — already RLS-protected; this spec adds a nullable `operator_run_id` column and an index. RLS policy unchanged.
1019: - **`SUBACCOUNT_OPERATOR_SETTINGS_WRITE`** — granted by default to `org_admin`. Used only by the PATCH route. The implementation chunk adds the key to the permissions registry, the role-default grant, and the permission-coverage CI gate.
1025: | Operator settings tab on AdminSubaccountDetailPage | `manager` and above (tab visible) | `org_admin` only (form enabled) |
1026: | Fresh-profile-restart per-task action | n/a (no read-only state) | `org_admin` only (button visible) |
1035: 1. **Three-way subaccount match** at chain-link start: `task.subaccount_id == credential.subaccount_id == profile.subaccount_id`. Mismatch → hard fail + incident.
1036: 2. **No cross-tenant adapter calls** — `operatorManagedBackend.dispatch()` reads `agent_runs.subaccount_id` once, sets the GUC via `setOrgGUC()`, and uses the same scoped tx for every subsequent read/write within the chain link.
1037: 3. **`operator_runs.organisation_id` AND `subaccount_id` are redundant with the FK chain** but kept on the row for RLS performance — Postgres applies the policy via these columns without a join.
1038: 4. **The pg-boss handlers re-read** the org/subaccount from the row they're processing and re-establish the GUC before any tenant-scoped write (the queue payload carries `operator_run_id`; the handler resolves the rest).
1039: 5. **The polling route** subaccount-checks via `setOrgGUC` + `getOrgScopedDb`; a row whose `subaccount_id` doesn't match the caller's principal returns 404 (NOT 403, to avoid leaking existence — consistent with the existing IEE route).
1050: 2. Set the GUC; resolve effective caps (`subaccountOperatorSettingsService.getEffectiveSettings(subaccountId)`).
1051: 3. Concurrency-cap check (FOR UPDATE on `operator_runs` filtered to running slots; transactional). If new task hitting cap → throw `OPERATOR_SESSION_LIMIT_EXCEEDED` (NOT queued, per § 3.17 item 5). If chain-continuation hitting cap → return a structured response that the chain-resume dispatcher handles by re-queueing (FIFO).
1053: 5. Resolve credential via `credentialBrokerService.requestOperatorSessionCredential` (or `resolveFallback` if stickiness is set).
1054: 6. Resolve / create profile via `operatorTaskProfileService.ensureActiveProfile(taskId, attemptNumber)`.
1056: 8. Call `sandboxExecutionService.runTask(...)` to start the sandbox session, injecting the credential and mounting the profile.
1060: A failure at any step (3–10) writes the chain-link row with status `'failed'` (or aborts before insert), emits the `operator.chain_link_start_failed` incident per § 3.17, and the chain-link dispatcher (§ 7.3) handles retry/backoff.
1062: ### 7.2 Chain-link terminal event — queued (pg-boss)
1064: When the sandbox session terminates (operator runtime emits a terminal step-state OR hard cap is reached OR cancel propagated OR runtime crashed), the adapter writes the chain-link row to its terminal status and enqueues `'operator-session-completed'` with payload `{ operatorRunId, agentRunId }`.
1070: 3. Inside `finalise()`: the adapter decides task-terminal vs paused-for-continuation (per § 3.14 item 4).
1071: 4. If task-terminal: parent agent run rolls up; cost rows are written via `operatorCostWriter.writeRowsForChainLink(operatorRunId)`; profile is scheduled for GC.
1072: 5. If paused-for-continuation: parent agent run sets `status='paused_for_chain_continuation'`; cost rows for THIS chain link are written via the same writer (per-chain-link cost rows happen regardless of pause/terminal); the chain-resume dispatcher enqueues `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` with payload `{ agentRunId }`.
1074: **Idempotency posture (per § 10.1):** key-based on `(operator_run_id, status)`. A re-delivery of the queue message is a no-op — the finaliser sees the row already in terminal state and returns the prior result.
1076: ### 7.3 Chain-link dispatch — queued (pg-boss) with backoff retry
1081: 2. If status is not `'paused_for_chain_continuation'` (or `'delegated'` on the first dispatch — bootstrap path), no-op.
1084: 5. On failure with `'transient'` failure class: increments a retry counter on the agent run (`operator_chain_failure_count`), enqueues a delayed re-dispatch (1 min → 5 min → 15 min via pg-boss's `startAfter` parameter).
1085: 6. On the 3rd consecutive failure: writes `agent_runs.status='paused_chain_failure'`, emits `'operator-session.task_paused_chain_failure'` event, sends user notification.
1086: 7. On failure with `'permanent' | 'auth' | 'profile_corruption'` failure class: bypasses the backoff and goes directly to `paused_chain_failure`.
1087: 8. Every failure (transient or permanent) emits an `operator.chain_link_start_failed` incident with `retry_attempt` and `is_terminal`.
1089: **Idempotency posture:** key-based on `(agentRunId, chain_seq_next)`. The chain_seq_next is computed from `max(chain_seq) + 1` for the task. Re-delivery of the queue message is a no-op when the chain link is already in `pending`/`running`/terminal state at that seq.
1091: ### 7.4 Progress events — queued (pg-boss) + WebSocket bridge
1093: Step-boundary events from the operator runtime are enqueued (`'operator-session-progressed'`) to keep the runtime's hot path off the DB. `operatorSessionProgressedHandler.ts`:
1098: The WebSocket bridge is best-effort: a dropped event is acceptable (the next event picks up the state). The polling fallback route is the durable visibility path.
1100: ### 7.5 Profile GC — queued (pg-boss cron)
1102: `operatorTaskProfileGcHandler.ts` is a 15-minute cron job that scans for `(status='scheduled_gc' AND scheduled_gc_at <= now())` rows, marks them `'gc_in_progress'`, deletes the underlying sandbox volume via the sandbox provider, then sets `'gc_done'`. Runs under `withAdminConnection` (cron-job principal) — does not require a tenant GUC because the scan is system-wide.
1104: **Idempotency:** key-based on `(profile_id, scheduled_gc_at)`. A re-run of the cron during deletion picks up only rows still in `'scheduled_gc'`; rows transitioned to `'gc_in_progress'` are skipped.
1106: ### 7.6 Cost-writer — inline within finaliser transaction
1108: The cost-writer is **NOT a separate queue**. It runs inline within the `finalise()` transaction triggered by `'operator-session-completed'`. This is intentional: the cost rows must commit atomically with the chain-link terminal status to avoid the "terminal-but-no-cost" or "cost-but-not-terminal" partial state.
1110: If the cost-writer fails: the entire `finalise()` transaction rolls back, the chain-link row stays in its prior state, and the pg-boss queue retries delivery. The cost-writer's own idempotency (key-based on `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)`) ensures the retry doesn't double-write.
1118: Single phase. **Phase 1** ships the whole Operator Backend end-to-end as defined here. The brief's D8 (chain-resume required, not a phase-3.5 deferral) and D11 (persistent profile required, not deferred) are honoured: no sub-phase splits the model.
1120: The implementation chunks in § 14 are sequential within Phase 1 but they are NOT phases — they are build-order ordering only. Each chunk leaves the system in a forward-compatible state (e.g. schema changes ship before the writers that depend on them).
1122: **Out-of-phase deferrals** (Phase 3.5 / Phase 5) are listed in § 11.
1128: 1. **No backward dependency.** Every column referenced by code in Chunk N is created in an equal-or-earlier chunk's migration. Verified via the dependency table in § 14.
1129: 2. **No orphaned deferrals.** Every "deferred" item is listed in § 11. Cross-checked.
1132: The implementation order is: schemas + migrations FIRST, then services FIRST among code, then routes, then UI, then renames + CS runbook + ADR + CI gates. Specific chunk ordering is in § 14.
1136: ### 10.1 Idempotency posture (per write path)
1141: | `operator_runs` terminal UPDATE | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status IN ('pending','running')`. 0 rows-affected = already terminal. |
1142: | `agent_runs` terminal UPDATE (task-terminal) | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status IN ('delegated','paused_*')` (the closed set of pre-terminal states). 0 rows-affected = already terminal; finaliser logs and returns 200 idempotent-hit. |
1143: | `agent_runs` pause UPDATE (`paused_for_chain_continuation`) | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status='delegated'`. 0 rows-affected = a concurrent path already paused or terminated. |
1144: | `operator_task_profiles` insert (first chain link) | **key-based** | unique constraint: `(task_id, attempt_number)`. 23505 → catch and return the existing row (idempotent-hit). |
1145: | `subaccount_operator_settings` UPSERT | **key-based** | PK: `subaccount_id`. Conflict → If-Match check (state-based concurrency control on top of key-based identity). |
1146: | `llm_requests` cost rows | **key-based** | unique index: `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)` for the new rows; existing `(agent_run_id, request_id)` for `per_token` rows. 23505 → idempotent-hit. |
1147: | pg-boss `'operator-session-completed'` enqueue | **key-based** | pg-boss singleton key: `'operator-session-completed:' || operator_run_id`. Re-enqueue is a no-op. |
1148: | pg-boss `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` enqueue | **key-based** | singleton key: `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link:' || agent_run_id || ':' || chain_seq_next`. |
1149: | pg-boss `'operator-task-profile-gc'` cron tick | **state-based** | the cron handler's `UPDATE WHERE status='scheduled_gc' AND scheduled_gc_at <= now() RETURNING id` is the eligibility predicate; concurrent ticks see disjoint row sets. |
1150: | Audit-event write | **non-idempotent (intentional)** | every action records its own audit row; replays are intentional duplicates so the audit log captures every attempted-action. |
1156: | `credentialBrokerService.requestOperatorSessionCredential` | **guarded** | broker enforces its own idempotency; safe to retry on network errors. |
1157: | `sandboxExecutionService.runTask` | **unsafe** | a retry could spawn a duplicate sandbox. Wrapped by the `operator_runs` state-based idempotency boundary (above). |
1158: | `operatorCostWriter.writeRowsForChainLink` | **safe** | key-based idempotent. Retry is a no-op. |
1159: | `recordIncident` | **safe** | Spec C / existing pattern — incident ingestor is internally idempotent. |
1161: | `operatorSessionDispatchNextChainLinkHandler` | **guarded** | wrapped by `operator_runs` (chain_seq) idempotency. |
1162: | `operatorTaskProfileGcHandler` | **guarded** | row-state predicate prevents double-delete. |
1163: | Profile-volume `delete` (Spec B provider call) | **unsafe** | a retry against a missing volume must be treated as success (the provider returns 404 → treat as `gc_done`). Wrapped by `operator_task_profiles.status` predicate. |
1170: | Two concurrent task-cancel callers | `agent_runs` UPDATE with optimistic predicate on the pre-terminal closed set. First wins; second gets 0 rows-affected and returns 409 with the current state. |
1172: | Two concurrent settings-PATCH calls | optimistic concurrency on `updated_at`. Second caller's `If-Match` mismatches → 409. |
1173: | Two concurrent finalises for the same chain link | the finaliser's `operator_runs` UPDATE optimistic predicate gives one winner. The cost-writer's key-based idempotency gives second a no-op. |
1175: | Fresh-profile-restart racing in-flight chain link | the restart route requires the current chain link to be `'failed'` or the task to be `'paused_chain_failure'`. Optimistic predicate: `UPDATE agent_runs SET ... WHERE status IN ('failed','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded','paused_for_chain_continuation')`. A `running` chain link blocks restart. |
1177: ### 10.4 Terminal event guarantees
1179: **Chain-link terminal events** (one per chain link):
1182: - Post-terminal prohibition: no further events with the same `chain_link_id` after a terminal event.
1183: - The terminal event's `status` is `'completed'` (with checkpoint OR final), `'failed'`, or `'cancelled'`. No `'partial'` at the chain-link level — partial completion of a chain link IS a `'completed'` with checkpoint (which is the normal case for non-final links).
1185: **Task terminal events** (one per task, only on true terminal states):
1188: - Post-terminal prohibition: no further events with the same `agent_run_id` after a terminal event.
1189: - Paused states emit `'operator-session.task_paused_*'` events; they are NOT terminal — multiple may fire over a task's life (pause → resume → pause → resume → terminal).
1196: - A task that hit the budget cap mid-chain-link → the chain link `'chain_link_completed'` with checkpoint; the task `'task_paused_budget_exceeded'` (NOT a silent partial on the task).
1198: - A fallback-engaged chain link → mixed cost rows per § 3.12; both row types reflect the boundary explicitly.
1205: | `operator_task_profiles (task_id, attempt_number) UNIQUE` | Concurrent ensure-profile | 23505 caught, idempotent-hit, returns existing row body to caller. (Internal route's HTTP equivalent: 200 idempotent.) |
1206: | `subaccount_operator_settings (subaccount_id) PK` | UPSERT conflict | normal UPSERT semantics (no HTTP exposure). |
1207: | `llm_requests (operator_run_id, source_type, boundary) UNIQUE` (new) | Cost-writer retry | 23505 caught, idempotent-hit, returns 200. |
1208: | `subaccount_operator_settings` If-Match mismatch | Stale write | 409 `OPERATOR_SETTINGS_CONFLICT` with `current_state` in body. |
1209: | Cancel a task already in terminal state | optimistic predicate 0 rows | 409 `TASK_ALREADY_TERMINAL` with `current_status` in body. |
1210: | Fresh-profile-restart on running chain link | optimistic predicate 0 rows | 409 `OPERATOR_TASK_RESTART_BLOCKED` with `current_status` and `active_chain_link_id` in body. |
1215: ### 10.7 State machine closures (`operator_runs`, `agent_runs`)
1219: Valid transitions:
1223: pending → failed           (dispatch failure — auth, profile, runtime unavailable)
1225: running → completed        (operator runtime terminal-success OR checkpoint-ready)
1226: running → failed           (operator runtime crash OR heartbeat stale OR auth lost without fallback OR hard-cap unresumable)
1231: - Any transition from `completed | failed | cancelled` (terminal).
1237: Valid transitions (operator-managed paths only):
1241: delegated → paused_for_chain_continuation            (chain link completed with checkpoint, task not done)
1242: paused_for_chain_continuation → delegated            (next chain link dispatched)
1243: delegated → paused_chain_failure                     (3 consecutive dispatch failures)
1244: paused_chain_failure → delegated                     (user retried)
1245: delegated → paused_budget_exceeded                   (budget cap hit)
1246: paused_budget_exceeded → delegated                   (user extended budget)
1249: {pending | delegated | paused_*} → cancelled         (user cancelled)
1253: - Any transition from `completed | failed | cancelled` (terminal).
1255: - `paused_* → completed | failed` without re-entering `delegated` (a paused task MUST resume to dispatch a chain link before it can produce a task-terminal status).
1257: Enforcement: optimistic predicates on every writer (§ 10.1, § 10.3). No DB-level CHECK on transition graph (Postgres doesn't support state-machine constraints declaratively); the writer-level predicates are the enforcement.
1260: 1. Add the value to the migration AND the union/type-annotation in the schema file.
1265: ## 11. Deferred items
1267: Single source of truth. Every "deferred", "later", "future", "Phase 3.5", "Phase 5" reference in this spec corresponds to a line below.
1271: - **Routing policy / cost-aware dispatch between Operator Backend and Native adapters.** Phase 3.5 — separate spec.
1272: - **"Cost savings vs API" customer-facing dashboard.** Phase 3.5. V1 surfaces cost in existing usage views only.
1278: - **Per-subaccount profile-size-cap configuration.** V1 has a system-wide 500 MB constant (§ 3.15 item 3). If customer demand surfaces, future spec adds it to `subaccount_operator_settings`.
1279: - **Cross-attempt comparison view in Run Trace.** § 3.15 item 7 / § 3.11 — V1 renders attempts as collapsed groups; a side-by-side compare view is deferred.
1280: - **In-flight settings hot-application.** V1 snapshots caps at chain-link dispatch time; in-flight chain links use the snapshot. A future spec could push settings changes to a running chain link (the operator runtime would need a "soft re-cap" signal). Deferred — operationally complex, low demand.
1281: - **In-memory slot-allocator cache** for concurrency-cap checks. V1 always queries the DB with FOR UPDATE. A future optimisation could cache slot counts in Redis if hot-path performance becomes a concern. Deferred — premature.
1288: - **Pure-function tests authored alongside the code.** Pure helpers in `*Pure.ts` files get vitest pure-function tests (`*Pure.test.ts`) covering happy path + at least one edge case per branch. Pure helpers that matter most: state-mapping (chain-link → task), retry-counter logic, settings snapshot extraction, idempotency-key derivation, profile-retention math, fallback-stickiness rules.
1289: - **RLS contract tests.** New tables added to `rlsProtectedTables.ts` are picked up by existing `verify-rls-coverage.sh` / `verify-rls-contract-compliance.sh` automatically. The existing `rls.context-propagation.test.ts` covers the default-deny posture — no new harness needed.

1317: | `r3-opentaskview-operator-completed.html` | Terminal-completed state of existing TaskHeader + ChatPane + Files tab. Cost summary is a 3-line inline footer in ActivityPane — see § 3.12. |

1630: These do NOT block spec acceptance. They are surfaced to the operator for visibility; the build session may resolve them as it implements.
1632: 1. **Vendor product name (pinned in Dockerfile only).** The spec does not state the specific vendor operator product or pinned version. The build chunk that authors `infra/sandbox-templates/operator-session/Dockerfile` selects the vendor and pinned version. Recommend the vendor used by the existing `openclaw-session` template (the rename preserves the pinned version unless explicitly bumped).
1634: 2. **`per_token` row schema linkage to `operator_run_id`.** Spec C did not extend `llm_requests` with an `operator_run_id` column (only `agent_run_id`). § 4.10 / Chunk 1 add this column. If the existing `llm_requests` writer has a Zod schema that closes off unknown fields, the writer's schema also needs updating in Chunk 5. The implementation chunk verifies before writing.
1636: 3. **Conversation-history per-link artefact format.** § 3.14 item 6 names "an artefact in the existing artefact store" but doesn't pin a specific MIME / Zod schema. The build chunk picks a JSONB shape consistent with existing operator-session-style artefacts (the same shape the IEE adapter uses for transcript-style artefacts, if one exists; otherwise a new shape registered in `shared/types/artefacts.ts`).
1638: 4. **`is_resumable_now` signal source.** § 3.14 item 3 names a boolean the operator runtime emits. The exact emission mechanism (step-state field vs separate signal vs in-band tool call) depends on the vendor product. Build chunk pins.
1640: 5. **Status-pill colour vs auto-extend banner colour clash.** § 3.4 + mockup `r15` show amber for auto-extend and amber for `paused_*` states. The UI implementation must disambiguate (e.g. label text differs; the indicator next to the pill carries the chain-link sub-state). Build chunk picks.
1642: 6. **Plan-tier display in `r11` Connections suspended state.** Mockup `r11-connections-suspended-state.html` shows "Suspended by OpenAI". The vendor codename SHOULD NOT appear in customer-facing copy (per § 3.1 naming discipline). Recommend: "Suspended" only, with the provider name coming from the broker envelope's `provider` field if the provider has a customer-facing display name reserved (Spec C territory). Build chunk verifies the broker exposes a non-codename display string OR the UI defaults to "Suspended" without naming the provider.

981: ## 6. Permissions / RLS checklist
982: 
983: Three new tenant-scoped tables. Each MUST have the four requirements from `docs/spec-authoring-checklist.md Â§ 4` (RLS policy, manifest entry, route guard, principal-scoped context).
984: 
985: ### 6.1 `operator_runs`
986: 
987: | Requirement | Status |
988: |---|---|
989: | **RLS policy** | Included in migration `0327_create_operator_runs.sql`. Standard org+subaccount scoping via the existing `current_setting('app.organisation_id')` and `current_setting('app.subaccount_id')` GUCs. `FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` enabled (defeats owner-bypass). Pattern matches `agent_runs` and `iee_runs`. |
990: | **Manifest entry** | Added to `server/config/rlsProtectedTables.ts` in the same migration. `{ tableName: 'operator_runs', schemaFile: 'operatorRuns.ts', policyMigration: '0327_create_operator_runs.sql', rationale: 'Chain-link state for operator-managed backend; one row per chain link; tenant-scoped by org+subaccount.' }`. |
991: | **Route guard** | Reads go through `GET /api/operator-sessions/:operatorRunId/progress` â€” guards: `authenticate`, `requirePermission('AGENT_RUN_READ')`, and `setOrgGUC()` before the query. Direct-DB-access prohibition is enforced by `verify-rls-contract-compliance.sh`. |
992: | **Principal-scoped context** | The adapter's `dispatch()`/`finalise()` run inside the existing agent-execution principal context (`PrincipalContext`). The chain-link writer uses `withOrgTx` for every write, propagating the org GUC. |
993: 
994: ### 6.2 `operator_task_profiles`
995: 
996: | Requirement | Status |
997: |---|---|
998: | **RLS policy** | Included in migration `0328_create_operator_task_profiles.sql`. Same shape as `operator_runs`. |
999: | **Manifest entry** | Added to `rlsProtectedTables.ts` in the same migration. Rationale: "Persistent browser-profile metadata per operator task; tenant-scoped." |
1000: | **Route guard** | The fresh-profile-restart route (`POST /api/operator-tasks/:agentRunId/fresh-profile-restart`) guards: `authenticate`, `requirePermission('AGENT_RUN_ADMIN')` (org-admin equivalent for this action), `setOrgGUC()`. The debug-retention-extend route reuses the same guard set. |
1001: | **Principal-scoped context** | Profile-volume mount runs inside the adapter principal context. The GC job runs under a maintenance principal (existing `withAdminConnection` pattern for cron-like jobs) â€” see Â§ 7. |
1002: 
1003: ### 6.3 `subaccount_operator_settings`
1004: 
1005: | Requirement | Status |
1006: |---|---|
1007: | **RLS policy** | Included in migration `0329_create_subaccount_operator_settings.sql`. Org+subaccount scoping. |
1008: | **Manifest entry** | Added to `rlsProtectedTables.ts` in the same migration. Rationale: "Per-subaccount operator runtime caps; tenant-scoped; org_admin write, manager read." |
1009: | **Route guard** | `GET /api/subaccounts/:subaccountId/operator-settings` â†’ `authenticate`, `requirePermission('SUBACCOUNT_READ')`, `resolveSubaccount`, `setOrgGUC()`. `PATCH` â†’ `authenticate`, `requirePermission('SUBACCOUNT_OPERATOR_SETTINGS_WRITE')`, `resolveSubaccount`, `setOrgGUC()`. The PATCH permission key is new in this spec â€” added to the permissions registry and the org-admin role's default grant. |
1010: | **Principal-scoped context** | All reads through the adapter use the existing principal context's `subaccountId` for row lookup. Defaulting (no row exists) returns the column defaults; the first write inserts. |
1011: 
1012: ### 6.4 Other touched tables
1013: 
1014: - **`agent_runs`** â€” already RLS-protected; this spec only extends the `status` enum and does not change RLS policy.
1015: - **`llm_requests`** (or canonical cost-ledger table) â€” already RLS-protected; this spec adds a nullable `operator_run_id` column and an index. RLS policy unchanged.

1018:

1022: 
1023: | UI surface | Read | Edit |
1024: |---|---|---|

1027: | Budget extension modal | task-assigned user + `manager` and above can extend | n/a (read-only) |
1028: | Concurrency-limit modal | task-creating user + same as above | n/a |

1032: 
1033: ### 6.7 Tenant-isolation invariants (defence in depth)
1034: 
1035: 1. **Three-way subaccount match** at chain-link start: `task.subaccount_id == credential.subaccount_id == profile.subaccount_id`. Mismatch â†’ hard fail + incident.
1036: 2. **No cross-tenant adapter calls** â€” `operatorManagedBackend.dispatch()` reads `agent_runs.subaccount_id` once, sets the GUC via `setOrgGUC()`, and uses the same scoped tx for every subsequent read/write within the chain link.
1037: 3. **`operator_runs.organisation_id` AND `subaccount_id` are redundant with the FK chain** but kept on the row for RLS performance â€” Postgres applies the policy via these columns without a join.
1038: 4. **The pg-boss handlers re-read** the org/subaccount from the row they're processing and re-establish the GUC before any tenant-scoped write (the queue payload carries `operator_run_id`; the handler resolves the rest).
1039: 5. **The polling route** subaccount-checks via `setOrgGUC` + `getOrgScopedDb`; a row whose `subaccount_id` doesn't match the caller's principal returns 404 (NOT 403, to avoid leaking existence â€” consistent with the existing IEE route).

858: ### 4.11 Source-of-truth precedence
859: 
860: Where the same fact has more than one representation, the read path is:
861: 
862: | Fact | Representations | Read priority |
863: |---|---|---|
864: | Chain-link terminal status | `operator_runs.status`, `'operator-session.chain_link_*'` event, finaliser log | `operator_runs.status` > event > log |
865: | Task terminal status | `agent_runs.status`, `'operator-session.task_*'` event, finaliser log | `agent_runs.status` > event > log |
866: | Chain-link wall-clock minutes | `(completed_at - started_at)`, the `sandbox_compute` ledger row's `wall_clock_ms` | DB timestamps win (per Â§ 3.17 item 4 DB-anchored discipline) |
867: | Effective per-subaccount caps | `subaccount_operator_settings` row, `operator_runs.checkpoint_payload.settings_snapshot` (if pinned) | `operator_runs`-pinned snapshot for an in-flight chain link; current settings for new dispatches |
868: | Conversation history | per-link artefacts vs `checkpoint_payload.last_action_summary` | artefacts win (the summary is an operator hint) |
869: | Profile-volume location | `operator_runs.profile_volume_id` (cached pointer), `operator_task_profiles.volume_id` (canonical) | `operator_task_profiles.volume_id` wins; the cached pointer is invalidated if `operator_task_profiles.attempt_number > operator_runs.attempt_number` |
870: | Concurrent-session slot count | `count(*) FROM operator_runs WHERE status='running' AND ...`, the slot-allocator's in-memory cache (if any) | DB query under `FOR UPDATE` always wins; no in-memory cache is permitted in V1 |

243: ### 3.5 Sandbox template (`operator-session`)
244: 
245: - **Template path:** `infra/sandbox-templates/operator-session/`. Single source of truth for both e2b (template) and `docker-compose` (local dev).
246: - **Rename from `openclaw-session`.** The current branch already carries `infra/sandbox-templates/openclaw-session/`. This spec renames that directory to `operator-session` in the same change-set. Files renamed: `Dockerfile`, `entrypoint.sh`, `README.md`, `CURRENT_VERSION`. Image-tag references in `operator_runs.image_tag`, the CI publish job (`.github/workflows/publish-sandbox-templates.yml`), and any docker-compose service name are updated. Git history preserves the rename via `git mv`.
247: - **Image contents.** The vendor operator runtime (pinned version), the model-invocation CLI it ships with, runtime dependencies. The spec author pins the specific vendor product and version inside the Dockerfile; the codename is local to this file only.
248: - **CI rebuild.** Reuses Spec B's image-build pipeline. Republishes when the Dockerfile or pinned vendor version changes.
249: - **Pinned per chain link.** `operator_runs.image_tag` records the specific image used. In-flight chain links complete on their original image when the vendor releases a new version; only new chain links get the new image. **In particular: a single task's chain links can run on different image tags** (link 1 on tag `v1.4.2`, link 17 on tag `v1.5.0` after a republish). The cost ledger and Run Trace record the image tag per chain link.
250: - **Mount points.** The persistent browser profile volume (Â§ 3.15) mounts at the browser's `user-data-dir` path on chain-link start. The Spec B sandbox isolation policy applies â€” adapter MUST assert task-subaccount matches credential-subaccount before mounting.
251: ### 3.6 Credential injection (broker abstraction)
252: 
253: - Adapter calls `credentialBrokerService.requestOperatorSessionCredential({ subaccountId, agentRunId })` at chain-link start.
254: - The broker returns an `OperatorSessionEnvelope` (Spec C contract) when usable, OR signals "unavailable" via the contract's existing failure mode. Raw tokens never leave the broker.
255: - **Subaccount-match assertion (defence in depth).** Before injection, the adapter asserts the returned credential's subaccount matches the `agent_runs.subaccount_id` AND `operator_runs.subaccount_id`. Mismatch is a hard fail with typed error `OPERATOR_SUBACCOUNT_MISMATCH`; chain-link status `failed`; incident emitted via `recordIncident()` with `failure_class: 'permanent'` (not a transient â€” points to a broker bug or a config drift, not a network hiccup).
256: - **What flows into the sandbox.** Only the redacted envelope's `credentialId` reference + the minimal start-time injection the operator runtime needs. The adapter MUST NOT log, persist, or print envelope contents in app logs.
257: - **What the adapter MAY consume from the envelope.** The redacted `authType` (which it maps 1:1 to `credential_mode`), the `planTier` (for cost-attribution context only), and the `usabilityState` (which is asserted to be `'connected_usable'` before injection; any other state is a hard fail with typed error `OPERATOR_SESSION_NOT_USABLE`). The adapter MUST NOT inspect `provider`-specific shapes â€” those live inside the broker.
258: 
259: ### 3.7 Operator-session â†’ API-key fallback
260: 
261: The single biggest production-readiness item. Without it, a rate-limit or suspension mid-run is a silent failure or a hard error with no graceful path.
262: 
263: 1. **Failure detection â€” closed signal set.** The operator runtime + CLI surface errors classified by the adapter as `session_unavailable` when ANY of:
264:    - HTTP `401`/`403` with provider-specific bodies indicating revocation/suspension/scope-stripped (concrete patterns enumerated in `operatorRuntimeErrors.ts`).
265:    - HTTP `429` with `Retry-After` â‰¥ 60s OR the provider's "session suspended" payload.
266:    - Broker refresh failure with `expired_refresh_token | provider_revoked | insufficient_scope` (Spec C classifications).
267:    - Connection-level errors > 3 consecutive retries against the operator runtime.
268: 
269: 2. **Fallback resolution.** Adapter calls `credentialBrokerService.resolveFallback({ subaccountId, agentRunId, originalCredentialId })`. The broker returns `{ envelope: OperatorSessionEnvelope-or-ApiKeyEnvelope, mode: 'operator_session' | 'api_key' } | null`. (Spec C reserved this seam; the spec author wires the broker side in the same chunk that wires the adapter side.)
270: 
271: 3. **Mid-run credential swap.** When fallback exists, the adapter:
272:    - Pauses the operator runtime via its in-band pause signal (vendor-specific; concrete API named in the implementation chunk).
273:    - Hot-swaps credentials inside the running sandbox via the same injection seam used at chain-link start.
274:    - Resumes; retries the failing turn once.
275:    - Emits `operator-session.fallback_engaged` lifecycle event (Â§ 4.7) with `chain_link_id`, `from_mode: 'operator_session'`, `to_mode: 'api_key'`, `reason: <failure-class>`, `step_index`.
276:    - Sets `operator_runs.credential_mode = 'api_key'` for the remainder of this chain link.
277: 
278: 4. **Hard-fail path.** If fallback resolution returns `null`, the chain link fails with typed error `OPERATOR_SESSION_UNAVAILABLE`. The chain-link row is written `status='failed', failure_reason='OPERATOR_SESSION_UNAVAILABLE'`. The customer sees the modal `r9-modal-operator-unavailable.html` pattern surfaced over the existing task surface (canonical component path chosen by the implementation chunk).
279: 
280: 5. **Cost-ledger semantics on mid-run swap.** The same chain link may produce **two** cost rows of the `credential_mode` boundary type: one `subscription_mediated` row for the pre-swap turns (`step_count` = turns up to swap) and one `per_token` row via the normal `llm_requests` path for the post-swap turns. Spec Â§ 3.12 enumerates the attribution rules in full.
281: 
282: 6. **Fallback stickiness across chain links.** Once fallback engages in chain link N, it is **sticky for the logical task**: chain link N+1 starts with `credential_mode = 'api_key'`, NOT a re-attempt of the operator-session credential. Stickiness clears when:
283:    - The broker emits `operator-session.usability_restored` (Spec C reserved this signal; the broker side is wired in this spec).
284:    - OR the user manually retries via "Refresh credential and resume" (a per-task action; the implementation chunk binds the audit event `task.operator.credential_refreshed`).
285:    Absent either signal, fallback persists for the remainder of the task. Run Trace renders the `fallback_engaged` event once at the chain-link boundary where it first applied; subsequent chain links inheriting fallback show a passive `credential_mode: api_key` indicator without re-emitting the lifecycle event.
286: 
287: ### 3.8 Token-lifecycle handling mid-session
288: 
289: - Adapter proactively triggers `credentialBrokerService.refresh({ credentialId })` at `expiresAt - REFRESH_LEAD_TIME_MS` (default 60s; configured via env, not per-subaccount).
290: - If a token expires mid-LLM-call inside the sandbox: the operator runtime surfaces a typed `auth_expired` signal; adapter triggers refresh, swaps the credential in-band, retries the failing turn once.
291: - If refresh fails with `expired_refresh_token | provider_revoked | insufficient_scope` (Spec C classifications): the broker marks the credential `revoked`; adapter routes through Â§ 3.7 fallback resolution.
292: - Refresh failures are typed lifecycle events `operator-session.refresh_failed` (Â§ 4.7) but are NOT incidents on their own â€” only the resulting chain-link-start-failure (Â§ 3.17) triggers an incident if the failure is not recovered by fallback.
293: 
294: ### 3.9 Mid-session progress visibility
295: 
296: Two layers, mirroring the existing IEE pattern:
297: 
298: - **Session-level events (push).** Operator runtime step boundaries surface to the adapter; the adapter:
299:   1. Bumps `operator_runs.last_progress_at = now()` and increments `step_count`.
300:   2. Enqueues a `'operator-session-progressed'` pg-boss event payload `{ runId, chainLinkId, stepIndex, summary, timestamp }`.
301:   3. The pg-boss handler bridges to the WebSocket `agent-run:{runId}` room via `emitAgentRunUpdate(runId, 'operator-session.progressed', payload)`.
302: 
303: - **Polling fallback (pull).** `GET /api/operator-sessions/:operatorRunId/progress` returns the latest progress snapshot from the `operator_runs` row. Route mirrors `server/routes/iee.ts:GET /api/iee/runs/:ieeRunId/progress`. Same auth gates: `authenticate`, `requirePermission('AGENT_RUN_READ')`, subaccount scoping via `getOrgScopedDb()`.
304: 
305: The polling route exists because (a) the WebSocket bridge can be down without the run being broken, and (b) some agent-run consumers don't keep a socket open. The brief is explicit that V1 keeps polling as the visibility primitive; streaming progress is deferred to Phase 3.5.
306: 
307: ### 3.10 Cancellation (chain-aware)
308: 
309: The adapter declares `'cancellation'` capability. Spec A's contract gives one method: `cancel({ runId, backendTaskId })`. The Operator Backend's implementation order at the **chain-link level**:
310: 
311: 1. **Operator runtime native hook.** If the runtime exposes a cancel endpoint (vendor-specific), the adapter calls it first.
312: 2. **Per-step-boundary check.** Adapter sets a cancel flag on the chain-link row; the operator runtime checks the flag at each step boundary and exits cleanly.
313: 3. **Heartbeat-stale backstop.** Spec A's shared reconcile loop catches chain links stuck in `running` with `last_progress_at` older than `HEARTBEAT_STALE_MS` (default 5 minutes) and marks them `failed` with `failure_reason='heartbeat_stale'`.
314: 
315: **Task-level cancellation semantics** are chain-aware. When a user cancels a task:
316: 
317: 1. **Cancel the active chain link** â€” writes `operator_runs.status = 'cancelled'` (only if currently `'pending' | 'running'`; otherwise no-op).
318: 2. **Drain queued chain-continuation jobs** â€” remove FIFO-queued continuation entries (Â§ 3.17 item 5) for this task from the scheduler queue. Atomic with step 3.
319: 3. **Prevent further chain dispatch** â€” set `agent_runs.status = 'cancelled'` via the optimistic predicate `UPDATE agent_runs SET status='cancelled' WHERE id = $1 AND status IN ('delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded','pending')`. 0 rows-affected means the task is already in a terminal state; return `409` with the current state.
320: 4. **Emit the task-terminal event** â€” `operator-session.task_cancelled` (Â§ 4.7). The finaliser performs full rollup.
321: 5. **Schedule profile retention/GC** â€” set `operator_task_profiles.scheduled_gc_at = now() + INTERVAL '48 hours'` per Â§ 3.15 item 4 (default retention).
322: 
323: Cancellation from a paused state follows the same task-level path: drain scheduler state, mark `agent_runs.status='cancelled'`, fire task-terminal event, schedule profile GC.
324: 
325: **Concurrency guard.** Steps 1, 2, 3 happen inside one `withOrgTx`-scoped transaction. If two concurrent cancels race, the first writes `status='cancelled'`; the second sees 0 rows-affected on step 3 and returns `409` to the losing caller. No double-emit of the terminal event.
326: ### 3.11 Run Trace integration
327: 
328: The adapter MUST emit Run Trace events for: session start, credential injected (auth-type redacted), each step boundary, fallback engaged (if any), chain-link terminal status, artefact harvest, task-terminal status (final chain link only).
329: 
330: Reuses the virtual-view Run Trace contract from the SynthetOS foundation refactor. New event-type families:
331: 
332: - `operator-session.*` (lifecycle): see Â§ 4.7.
333: - `operator.*` (incidents, audit, system): see Â§ 4.8, Â§ 4.9.
334: 
335: **Chain-link merged view.** Run Trace renders the chain as a single merged timeline with `chain link N starts` dividers (per mockup `r17-runtrace-chain-link-divider.html`). The renderer changes are scoped to `client/src/pages/operate/components/RunTraceEventRenderer.tsx` â€” a new `<ChainLinkDivider>` element inserts between events belonging to different `chain_seq` values.
336: 
337: **Attempt grouping.** When a task has `attempt_number > 1` (fresh-profile restart per Â§ 3.15 item 7), Run Trace renders attempts as **top-level groups** above the chain-link structure. Superseded attempts are collapsed by default; the current attempt is the default-expanded view. The merged-timeline view above spans only the current attempt; cross-attempt comparison is a separate (future) view.
338: 
339: **Sensitive content.** Checkpoint payloads (page URLs, screenshots) are NOT rendered in Run Trace by default â€” they live in `operator_runs.checkpoint_payload` and surface only through the harvested-artefact path (Â§ 3.12) when promoted. See Â§ 3.14 item 10 for the full policy.
340: 
341: ### 3.12 Per-customer cost visibility
342: 
343: Even when LLM cost is zero (subscription-prepaid), sandbox compute is real spend. The adapter writes to the cost ledger:
344: 
345: **A. Sandbox compute (real spend, every chain link).**
346: 
347: One `source_type: 'sandbox_compute'` row per chain link / sandbox session. Inputs taken from Spec B's `SandboxRunTaskOutput`: `vCPUSeconds`, `wallClockMs`, `peakMemoryBytes`. Cost is computed by the existing sandbox-compute pricing function (Spec B). The ledger row carries the chain link's `operator_run_id` and is joined to the parent task at read time via `agent_run_id`.
348: 
349: **B. Subscription-mediated (zero-cost accounting, per chain link).**
350: 
351: One `source_type: 'subscription_mediated'` row per chain link where `credential_mode = 'operator_session'`. Zero-cost. Carries:
352: 
353: | Field | Value |
354: |---|---|
355: | `source_type` | `'subscription_mediated'` |
356: | `cost_cents` | `0` |
357: | `agent_run_id` | parent task |
358: | `operator_run_id` | chain-link id |
359: | `chain_seq` | chain-link sequence number |
360: | `vendor_session_id` | the opaque vendor session id (audit) |
361: | `credential_mode` | `'operator_session'` |
362: | `step_count` | turns within this chain link |
363: | `plan_tier` | from the broker envelope (audit context) |
364: 
365: **C. Per-token (mid-run swap or fully-fallback chain link).**
366: 
367: When fallback engages mid-chain-link: turns BEFORE the swap â†’ counted in the chain link's `subscription_mediated` row (with `step_count` reflecting only the pre-swap turns); turns AFTER the swap â†’ flow through the normal `llm_requests` writer with `source_type: 'per_token'`. The boundary is recorded in the `operator-session.fallback_engaged` event payload.
368: 
369: When a full chain link runs under fallback (`credential_mode = 'api_key'` from chain-link start): NO `subscription_mediated` row is written; only `per_token` rows via `llm_requests`. The `sandbox_compute` row is still written.
370: 
371: **Aggregation:** dashboards use the existing usage views. The `(agent_run_id, source_type)` index on `llm_requests` (or equivalent) supports the rollup. **No new dashboard is built in V1** â€” data must be queryable from existing usage views.
372: 
373: **Idempotency posture (per Â§ 10.1):** all three writers are **key-based idempotent** on `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)`. A retry after partial commit MUST NOT double-write. The cost-writer is invoked exactly once per chain-link terminal event via the finaliser hook (Spec A pattern), not from the adapter's hot path. Boundary key for `subscription_mediated` is `(operator_run_id, 'subscription_mediated', 'chain_link')`. For `sandbox_compute`: `(operator_run_id, 'sandbox_compute', 'chain_link')`. For `per_token` rows that share a chain link with `subscription_mediated`: the existing `llm_requests` writer already keys on `(agent_run_id, request_id)`; this spec adds `operator_run_id` as a column on `llm_requests` (migration extends the existing schema).
374: 
375: **Concurrency guard (per Â§ 10.3):** the cost-writer holds an advisory lock on `(operator_run_id)` for the duration of the rollup transaction. Two concurrent finalises (rare; only possible if the pg-boss event handler retries before idempotency catches it) cannot interleave row writes.
376: 
377: ### 3.13 CS runbook for provider account suspension
378: 
379: Per Spec C Decision 3 risk #1: the customer will blame SynthetOS regardless of what they signed at opt-in. Before the first Plus-tier opt-in customer hits a suspension:
380: 
381: - **Runbook.** `docs/runbooks/operator-session-account-suspension.md`. Authored in this spec change-set. Sections:
382:   1. What "operator-session suspended" means (one paragraph, plain English).
383:   2. How the system detects suspension (the Â§3.7 closed signal set).
384:   3. The automatic notification chain (incident â†’ CS notification â†’ assigned user inbox + admin notification).
385:   4. How to retrieve the disclosure record by `consent_record_id` (Spec C).
386:   5. Comms templates (apology, fact-based, with disclosure link).
387:   6. Customer's options (reconnect, add fallback API key, cancel ongoing tasks).
388:   7. Escalation tree.
389: 
390: - **Comms templates.** `docs/runbooks/templates/operator-session-suspension-customer-email.md`, `.../in-app-message.md`. Plain English; refers to the disclosure record without legal jargon.
391: 
392: - **Automatic detection.** The Â§3.7 fallback path emits a typed `system-monitor` notification on the first `OPERATOR_SESSION_UNAVAILABLE` hit AND on `usability_state` flipping from `'connected_usable'` to anything else (broker-side change). The CS notification is the typed event `cs.operator_session.suspended_detected` consumed by the existing inbox pipeline.
393: 
394: Small artefact (one-pager + comms templates + the typed CS notification wiring) but it blocks first Plus-tier onboarding. Belongs in this change-set, not deferred â€” the moment the adapter ships to a Plus-tier customer, the runbook is on the critical path.
395: ### 3.14 Chain-resume model
396: 
397: A single operator task spans many 120-min chain-link sessions. Each session is a "chain link." When the soft cap approaches, the operator drives itself to a checkpoint, persists state, and the session ends. A scheduler picks up the task and dispatches the next chain link, which resumes from the checkpoint. The user sees one task progressing, not many separate runs.
398: 
399: 1. **Chain-link data model.** Locked in Â§ 3.3. `chain_seq` starts at 1; `parent_chain_link_id` FKs to the prior chain link; `checkpoint_payload` JSONB holds (or points to) the resume state.
400: 
401: 2. **Checkpoint contents (minimum).** Â§ 4.6 pins the JSONB shape. Required fields: `original_task_brief_ref`, `conversation_history_pointer` (artefact-store reference, not inline blob), `current_page_url`, `last_action_summary`, `next_planned_step`, `last_state_screenshot_artefact_id` (pointer; the screenshot lives in the artefact store).
402: 
403: 3. **Soft cap + auto-extend.**
404:    - Soft cap = `subaccount_operator_settings.session_soft_cap_minutes` (default 120, range 30â€“240, per Â§ 3.16).
405:    - At `T - 10 min`, the operator emits a `'preparing_checkpoint'` step-state signal. The adapter records `operator_runs.last_progress_at = now()` and propagates the signal via the WebSocket bridge.
406:    - If at the soft cap the operator's `is_resumable_now` boolean is `true`, the chain link terminates `'completed'` with `checkpoint_payload` non-null.
407:    - If `is_resumable_now` is `false` at the soft cap, the adapter auto-extends up to `subaccount_operator_settings.auto_extend_grace_minutes` (default 30, range 0â€“60, per Â§ 3.16).
408:    - At soft-cap + grace, the chain link terminates `'failed'` with `failure_reason='hard_cap_unresumable'` and `failed_mid_step=true`. The next chain link does not auto-dispatch â€” the task transitions to `paused_chain_failure` (per Â§ 3.17 item 1, treated like a dispatch failure for retry counting).
409: 
410: 4. **Chain-link dispatch.** End of chain link N writes `checkpoint_payload` and emits `'operator-session-completed'` (the standard adapter terminal event, with status `'completed'` and a non-null `checkpoint_payload` field â€” distinct from the task-terminal `'completed'`). The finaliser handler distinguishes:
411:    - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` AND the parent task is not at its max chain length â†’ dispatch next chain link via the `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` queue.
412:    - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` AND the parent task IS at max chain length â†’ task-terminal `'failed'` with `failure_reason='max_chain_length_reached'` (rolls up to `agent_runs.status='failed'`).
413:    - `completed` with NULL `checkpoint_payload` AND `is_resumable_now=true` on the last step AND task scope reports "done" â†’ task-terminal `'completed'`. (The operator runtime emits a `'task_completed'` step-state when the task is genuinely done; that signal sets the writer to NULL checkpoint and triggers task termination.)
414:    - `failed` with `failed_mid_step=true` â†’ task transitions to `paused_chain_failure`; user must retry or cancel.
415:    - `failed` with `failed_mid_step=false` â†’ propagate task-terminal `'failed'` (operator runtime hard error, e.g. crash).
416:    - `cancelled` â†’ propagate task-terminal `'cancelled'`.
417: 
418: 5. **Resume payload.** Chain link N+1 starts with: the original task brief, the accumulated conversation-history pointer, the checkpoint from chain link N, and the persistent browser profile (Â§ 3.15) mounted. The operator's first action is to verify it's on the expected page and continue from the `next_planned_step`.
419: 
420: 6. **Conversation history accumulation.** Per-chain-link blobs joined at read time, capped at last N chain links of context for the operator-model invocation. Concretely: each chain link writes a single artefact `operator-conversation-link-{operator_run_id}.json` to the existing artefact store. The resume payload composer reads the latest K (default 5) artefacts and concatenates them in chain order. K is a constant in `operatorConversationHistoryPure.ts`; not configurable per-subaccount in V1.
421: 
422: 7. **Terminal states + failure classification (runtime vs start).**
423:    - **Runtime failure** â€” chain link is in state `'running'` at the time of failure â†’ terminates the **task** with the chain link's failure reason (`agent_runs.status='failed'`). Remaining chain dispatch does NOT happen.
424:    - **Start failure** â€” chain link is in state `'pending'` at the time of failure (dispatch-time, before the chain link has begun running) â†’ Â§ 3.17 retry/pause semantics apply (backoff retry then `paused_chain_failure`), NOT immediate task termination.
425:    - The state-machine boundary is at `pending â†’ running`. The transition timestamp is `operator_runs.started_at` (set by the adapter immediately after the sandbox session is created and the credential is injected).
426: 
427: 8. **Run Trace.** Merged timeline with `chain link N starts` dividers (Â§ 3.11). The virtual-view contract spans chain links via the `agent_run_id` join.
428: 
429: 9. **TaskHeader status.** Mockup `r14-taskheader-chain-link-status.html`. Three variants:
430:    - Known estimate (after first handoff): `"link N of ~M, T hrs elapsed"`. `~M` is computed as `min(max_chain_length, max(N+2, ceil(estimated_total_steps / avg_steps_per_link)))` and refreshes per chain link.
431:    - Unknown estimate (before first handoff): `"link N of â€”"`. Tooltip explains "estimate available after the first chain handoff completes."
432:    - Terminal: `"{N} sessions, {H}h {M}m total"`.
433: 
434: 10. **Checkpoint-payload security.** Checkpoint payloads are sensitive task artefacts and MUST be:
435:     - **Encrypted at rest** where existing artefact infrastructure supports it. Concretely: the JSONB column is encrypted via the existing app-level encryption helper (the same helper used by `agent_run_payloads`'s redaction pipeline). If the helper is not yet wired for this column, the implementation chunk wires it.
436:     - **Scoped by org/subaccount/task.** The RLS policy on `operator_runs` enforces org+subaccount; the `task_id` (= `agent_run_id`) is implicit via the FK.
437:     - **Excluded from broad logs.** The adapter MUST NOT log `checkpoint_payload` contents at any log level. A grep gate (`scripts/gates/verify-no-checkpoint-logging.sh`) bans naive log calls referencing the column.
438:     - **Redacted in Run Trace by default.** The embedded screenshot is treated as an INTERNAL recovery artefact, not customer-visible. Customer-facing screenshots flow only through the harvested-artefact path (Â§ 3.12 / artefact harvester).
439: 
440: ### 3.15 Persistent browser profile per task
441: 
442: Smooth chain handoff requires browser state (cookies, login session, local storage) to survive across chain links. Without this, every chain link starts cold, must replay credentials, and breaks on MFA.
443: 
444: 1. **Profile storage â€” new table `operator_task_profiles`.**
445: 
446: | Column | Type | Notes |
447: |---|---|---|
448: | `id` | `uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid()` | |
449: | `task_id` | `uuid NOT NULL REFERENCES agent_runs(id) ON DELETE RESTRICT` | One profile per task. |
450: | `organisation_id` | `uuid NOT NULL` | RLS scope. |
451: | `subaccount_id` | `uuid NOT NULL` | RLS scope. |
452: | `attempt_number` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 1` | Bumps on fresh-profile restart (Â§ 3.15 item 7). |
453: | `volume_id` | `text NOT NULL` | Sandbox-volume id (opaque pointer; safe to log). |
454: | `size_bytes` | `bigint NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` | Updated on each chain link end. |
455: | `size_cap_bytes` | `bigint NOT NULL DEFAULT 524288000` | 500 MB default per Â§ 3.15 item 3. |
456: | `status` | `text NOT NULL CHECK (status IN ('active','scheduled_gc','gc_in_progress','gc_done'))` | Lifecycle. |
457: | `scheduled_gc_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | Set to `task_terminal_at + retention_window`. |
458: | `debug_retention_extended_by` | `uuid NULL REFERENCES users(id)` | Set when admin extends retention to 14 days. |
459: | `debug_retention_extended_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | Audit. |
460: | `created_at` | `timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()` | |
461: | `updated_at` | `timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()` | |
462: 
463: Unique constraint: `(task_id, attempt_number)`.
464: 
465: 2. **Profile mount.** The `operator-session` Docker template mounts the volume at the browser's `user-data-dir` path on chain-link start. Mount instruction is part of the template's `entrypoint.sh`.
466: 
467: 3. **Profile size cap.** Default 500 MB per task. Enforced by:
468:    - Disk-usage check before chain-link start (adapter reads `size_bytes`; if `size_bytes >= size_cap_bytes`, chain link fails with `failure_reason='profile_size_cap_exceeded'`).
469:    - Docker volume quota (template-level, set in entrypoint).
470:    Cap is a system constant, NOT per-subaccount in V1.
471: 
472: 4. **Profile lifecycle + retention.** Volume is created on first chain-link start (`status='active'`). Persists across chain links. After task-terminal: `status='scheduled_gc', scheduled_gc_at = now() + INTERVAL '48 hours'` (default). An admin (`org_admin`) may set `debug_retention_extended_by/_at` at task-terminal time, which extends `scheduled_gc_at` to `now() + INTERVAL '14 days'` for that task. Customer-visible artefacts (per Â§ 3.12) are harvested into the artefact store BEFORE the volume is GC'd, regardless of retention window. A pg-boss cron job (`operator-task-profile-gc`, every 15 minutes) marks profiles `status='gc_in_progress'` when `now() >= scheduled_gc_at`, performs the volume delete via the sandbox provider, then sets `status='gc_done'`. Hard max lifetime including retention = `max_wall_clock_per_task_days` + 14 days.
473: 
474: 5. **Profile permissions.** Volume access scoped to chain links of the owning task by Spec B's sandbox isolation primitive. The adapter MUST assert `task.subaccount_id == credential.subaccount_id == profile.subaccount_id` before mounting (defence in depth, three-way check). Mismatch â†’ hard fail with typed error `OPERATOR_PROFILE_SUBACCOUNT_MISMATCH`.
475: 
476: 6. **First-chain-link cold start.** First chain link gets a fresh `user-data-dir`. Login from the credential broker happens naturally in the model loop â€” no special bootstrap.
477: 
478: 7. **Failure recovery + fresh-profile restart.** If the profile volume is corrupted or unrecoverable, chain-link start fails with typed error `OPERATOR_PROFILE_UNRECOVERABLE` and Â§ 3.17 incident path engages. Authorised users (`org_admin`) may opt to "restart task with fresh profile" â€” a per-task action with the following LOCKED semantics:
479:    - **Same `agent_run_id`** (the customer-visible identity is preserved).
480:    - **New `attempt_number`** on every `operator_runs` row from this point (and a new `operator_task_profiles` row with the bumped attempt). Default starts at `1`; bumps on each fresh-profile restart.
481:    - **Conversation history resets at the attempt boundary.** Chain link 1 of attempt N+1 starts with the ORIGINAL task brief only.
482:    - **Old chain links retained but marked `superseded_by_attempt = N+1`.** Visible in Run Trace under a collapsed "Attempt 1" group; current attempt is the default-expanded view.
483:    - **Old profile retained per Â§ 3.15 item 4 retention rules** (default 48 hr after the attempt-superseded event; admin debug-retention extends to 14 days). The new attempt's volume is created fresh.
484:    - **Audit event** `task.operator.fresh_profile_restart` (Â§ 4.9) writes `actor_user_id`, `prior_attempt_number`, `new_attempt_number`, `prior_chain_seq_count`, `request_id`.
485:    - Run Trace renders attempts as top-level groups; chain links nest under their attempt.
486: 
487: ### 3.16 Per-subaccount operator settings
488: 
489: Runtime limits live on the subaccount, not on the org. Subaccounts are where agents run. A new "Operator" tab on `client/src/pages/AdminSubaccountDetailPage.tsx`, inserted between Board Config (`'board'`) and Usage & Costs (`'usage'`) in the `ActiveTab` union and `TAB_LABELS` map.
490: 
491: **Tab visibility:** `org_admin` can edit; `manager` can view; below `manager` cannot see the tab.
492: 
493: **Fields and defaults** (locked):
494: 
495: | Field | DB column | Default | Min | Max | UI section |
496: |---|---|---|---|---|---|
497: | Soft session cap (min) | `session_soft_cap_minutes` | 120 | 30 | 240 | Session limits |
498: | Auto-extend grace (min) | `auto_extend_grace_minutes` | 30 | 0 | 60 | Session limits |
499: | Max chain length | `max_chain_length` | 50 | 1 | 500 | Task limits |
500: | Max wall-clock per task (days) | `max_wall_clock_per_task_days` | 30 | 1 | 365 | Task limits |
501: | Per-task budget cap (op-session minutes) | `per_task_budget_cap_minutes` | 6000 | 60 | 60000 | Task limits |
502: | Concurrent operator sessions (per subaccount) | `concurrent_operator_sessions_cap` | 5 | 1 | 25 | Session limits |
503: 
504: **Storage choice.** A new tenant-scoped table `subaccount_operator_settings` (one row per subaccount; primary key `subaccount_id`). This is preferred over adding six columns to the existing `subaccounts` table â€” keeps the operator concern isolated, and is the same shape `subaccount_optimiser_settings` already uses for the Sub-account Optimiser feature.
505: 
506: | Column | Type | Notes |
507: |---|---|---|
508: | `subaccount_id` | `uuid PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES subaccounts(id) ON DELETE CASCADE` | |
509: | `organisation_id` | `uuid NOT NULL` | RLS scope (defence in depth). |
510: | `session_soft_cap_minutes` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 120 CHECK (session_soft_cap_minutes BETWEEN 30 AND 240)` | |
511: | `auto_extend_grace_minutes` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 30 CHECK (auto_extend_grace_minutes BETWEEN 0 AND 60)` | |
512: | `max_chain_length` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 50 CHECK (max_chain_length BETWEEN 1 AND 500)` | |
513: | `max_wall_clock_per_task_days` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 30 CHECK (max_wall_clock_per_task_days BETWEEN 1 AND 365)` | |
514: | `per_task_budget_cap_minutes` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 6000 CHECK (per_task_budget_cap_minutes BETWEEN 60 AND 60000)` | |
515: | `concurrent_operator_sessions_cap` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 5 CHECK (concurrent_operator_sessions_cap BETWEEN 1 AND 25)` | |
516: | `updated_at` | `timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()` | ETag source. |
517: | `updated_by_user_id` | `uuid NULL REFERENCES users(id)` | Audit. |
518: 
519: **Defaulting.** When a chain link reads its caps and no row exists for the subaccount, the read uses the column defaults. The first write inserts the row (UPSERT pattern). No backfill migration is needed; the row is created lazily.
520: 
521: **Optimistic concurrency.** Writes use `If-Match` against `updated_at` rounded to seconds (consistent with the JWT `iat` precision discipline from KNOWLEDGE.md). Mismatch returns `409 OPERATOR_SETTINGS_CONFLICT` with the current row body; UI MUST refetch and redisplay before retry.
522: 
523: **Server-side validation.** Each PATCH validates against the column CHECK constraints AND the explicit min/max in the table above (defence-in-depth â€” a future CHECK loosening cannot silently widen the API).
524: 
525: **Audit event.** Every successful update writes `subaccount.operator_settings.updated` (Â§ 4.9) with `before`, `after`, `actor_user_id`, `request_id`, `source` (`ui` | `api` | `system`).
526: 
527: **Settings application.** Changes apply to **new chain links only**. An in-flight chain link uses the cap that was in effect when it dispatched (snapshot pinned in the chain-link row at dispatch time â€” see Â§ 3.17 incident payload `settings_snapshot`). The UI surfaces a footer note: "Changes apply to new sessions only."
528: 
529: ### 3.17 Chain-link start failure + incident emission
530: 
531: A chain link can fail to dispatch for several reasons (auth lost, runtime unavailable, profile corrupted, subaccount over concurrency cap, budget cap hit).
532: 
533: 1. **Backoff retry on transient failure.** Chain-link dispatch is retried with exponential backoff: 1 min, 5 min, 15 min. After **3 consecutive failures**, the task transitions to `paused_chain_failure`.
534: 
535:    The retry counter resets on:
536:    - A user-initiated retry (via the per-task "Retry" action).
537:    - A successful chain-link dispatch (i.e. counter is "consecutive failures since last successful dispatch", not lifetime).
538: 
539: 2. **Incident emission.** Each retry attempt writes its own incident via `recordIncident()` (`server/services/incidentIngestor.ts`). Typed event: `operator.chain_link_start_failed`. Payload (locked shape â€” Â§ 4.8):
540: 
541:    ```json
542:    {
543:      "event": "operator.chain_link_start_failed",
544:      "organisation_id": "<uuid>",
545:      "subaccount_id": "<uuid>",
546:      "agent_run_id": "<uuid>",
547:      "operator_run_id": "<uuid|null>",
548:      "chain_seq": 7,
549:      "attempt_number": 1,
550:      "failure_class": "transient|permanent|budget|concurrency|profile_corruption|auth",
551:      "failure_reason": "<verbatim error string>",
552:      "request_id": "<correlation id>",
553:      "credential_mode": "operator_session|api_key|unknown",
554:      "profile_volume_id": "<opaque pointer or null>",
555:      "settings_snapshot": {
556:        "session_soft_cap_minutes": 120,
557:        "auto_extend_grace_minutes": 30,
558:        "max_chain_length": 50,
559:        "per_task_budget_cap_minutes": 6000,
560:        "concurrent_operator_sessions_cap": 5
561:      },
562:      "retry_attempt": 2,
563:      "is_terminal": false
564:    }
565:    ```
566: 
567:    `is_terminal=true` is set on the 3rd consecutive failure that triggers `paused_chain_failure`. The system-monitoring agent owns: classifying repeated patterns across tasks (e.g. "all chain links failing on subaccount X with the same auth error" â†’ suggest re-auth flow), flagging remedies, escalating to the assigned user or org admin when an automated remedy is not available.
568: 
569: 3. **User notification.** On `paused_chain_failure` transition, notify the assigned user via the existing inbox/notification path. Notification payload includes the failure class and the suggested action (Retry / Cancel). User actions:
570:    - **Retry** â€” resets retry counter, dispatches next chain link from the current checkpoint (no fresh profile). Audit event `task.operator.chain_failure_retried`.
571:    - **Cancel** â€” Â§ 3.10 cancellation path.
572: 
573: 4. **Budget-cap auto-pause and accounting.** Hitting the per-task budget cap is NOT a failure â€” it is a deliberate auto-pause. Task transitions to `paused_budget_exceeded`.
574: 
575:    **Accounting rules:**
576:    - Minutes consumed are measured using **DB-anchored timestamps** (`sandbox_started_at` / `sandbox_completed_at` written by the adapter from `now()` inside the chain-link transaction). NOT app-process wall-clock.
577:    - Consumption is the **actual sandbox wall-clock minutes** elapsed, not the allocated cap. A 90-minute chain link consumes 90 minutes.
578:    - When consumption hits the per-task budget cap mid-chain-link, the running chain link MUST checkpoint and pause at the **next resumable boundary** (NOT hard-kill), UNLESS the chain link also breaches the hard safety limit (soft cap + grace), in which case it terminates per Â§ 3.14 item 3 hard-cap behaviour.
579:    - Budget extension actions are additive (`new_cap = old_cap + extension_minutes`), never absolute resets, and write `task.operator_budget.extended` (Â§ 4.9) with `actor_user_id`, `extension_minutes`, `request_id`, `source`.
580:    - The user can extend at increments of 60 minutes (UI offers presets +1000, +3000, plus a custom-amount input bounded 60..60000 with 60-min step per mockup `r16-modal-budget-exceeded-autopause.html`).
581: 
582: 5. **Concurrency-cap behaviour â€” distinguish new-task vs chain-continuation.**
583: 
584:    The `concurrent_operator_sessions_cap` per subaccount is computed at dispatch time as `count of operator_runs WHERE subaccount_id=$1 AND status='running' AND superseded_by_attempt IS NULL`. The slot accounting is row-level under `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE` to prevent two concurrent dispatches racing past the cap.
585: 
586:    - **New user-requested operator task over the cap:** REJECTED at task-create / first-dispatch with typed error `OPERATOR_SESSION_LIMIT_EXCEEDED`. Customer-facing message surfaced via the existing task-create / operator-capacity modal (canonical component path chosen by the implementation chunk; the mockup `r8-modal-concurrency-limit.html` documents the intended pattern). NOT queued. NOT an incident.
587:    - **Existing chain-continuation hitting the cap mid-task:** QUEUED FIFO on the new `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` pg-boss queue. Task state stays `paused_for_chain_continuation`. Dispatched when a slot frees. NOT an incident â€” normal flow control.
588: 
589:    The distinction matters: new tasks fail-fast so the user can address the cap immediately; in-flight tasks defer so a busy moment doesn't kill long-running work.

403: 3. **Soft cap + auto-extend.**
404:    - Soft cap = `subaccount_operator_settings.session_soft_cap_minutes` (default 120, range 30â€“240, per Â§ 3.16).
405:    - At `T - 10 min`, the operator emits a `'preparing_checkpoint'` step-state signal. The adapter records `operator_runs.last_progress_at = now()` and propagates the signal via the WebSocket bridge.
406:    - If at the soft cap the operator's `is_resumable_now` boolean is `true`, the chain link terminates `'completed'` with `checkpoint_payload` non-null.
407:    - If `is_resumable_now` is `false` at the soft cap, the adapter auto-extends up to `subaccount_operator_settings.auto_extend_grace_minutes` (default 30, range 0â€“60, per Â§ 3.16).
408:    - At soft-cap + grace, the chain link terminates `'failed'` with `failure_reason='hard_cap_unresumable'` and `failed_mid_step=true`. The next chain link does not auto-dispatch â€” the task transitions to `paused_chain_failure` (per Â§ 3.17 item 1, treated like a dispatch failure for retry counting).
409: 
410: 4. **Chain-link dispatch.** End of chain link N writes `checkpoint_payload` and emits `'operator-session-completed'` (the standard adapter terminal event, with status `'completed'` and a non-null `checkpoint_payload` field â€” distinct from the task-terminal `'completed'`). The finaliser handler distinguishes:
411:    - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` AND the parent task is not at its max chain length â†’ dispatch next chain link via the `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` queue.
412:    - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` AND the parent task IS at max chain length â†’ task-terminal `'failed'` with `failure_reason='max_chain_length_reached'` (rolls up to `agent_runs.status='failed'`).
413:    - `completed` with NULL `checkpoint_payload` AND `is_resumable_now=true` on the last step AND task scope reports "done" â†’ task-terminal `'completed'`. (The operator runtime emits a `'task_completed'` step-state when the task is genuinely done; that signal sets the writer to NULL checkpoint and triggers task termination.)
414:    - `failed` with `failed_mid_step=true` â†’ task transitions to `paused_chain_failure`; user must retry or cancel.
415:    - `failed` with `failed_mid_step=false` â†’ propagate task-terminal `'failed'` (operator runtime hard error, e.g. crash).
416:    - `cancelled` â†’ propagate task-terminal `'cancelled'`.
417: 
418: 5. **Resume payload.** Chain link N+1 starts with: the original task brief, the accumulated conversation-history pointer, the checkpoint from chain link N, and the persistent browser profile (Â§ 3.15) mounted. The operator's first action is to verify it's on the expected page and continue from the `next_planned_step`.
419: 
420: 6. **Conversation history accumulation.** Per-chain-link blobs joined at read time, capped at last N chain links of context for the operator-model invocation. Concretely: each chain link writes a single artefact `operator-conversation-link-{operator_run_id}.json` to the existing artefact store. The resume payload composer reads the latest K (default 5) artefacts and concatenates them in chain order. K is a constant in `operatorConversationHistoryPure.ts`; not configurable per-subaccount in V1.
421: 
422: 7. **Terminal states + failure classification (runtime vs start).**
423:    - **Runtime failure** â€” chain link is in state `'running'` at the time of failure â†’ terminates the **task** with the chain link's failure reason (`agent_runs.status='failed'`). Remaining chain dispatch does NOT happen.
424:    - **Start failure** â€” chain link is in state `'pending'` at the time of failure (dispatch-time, before the chain link has begun running) â†’ Â§ 3.17 retry/pause semantics apply (backoff retry then `paused_chain_failure`), NOT immediate task termination.
425:    - The state-machine boundary is at `pending â†’ running`. The transition timestamp is `operator_runs.started_at` (set by the adapter immediately after the sandbox session is created and the credential is injected).
426: 
427: 8. **Run Trace.** Merged timeline with `chain link N starts` dividers (Â§ 3.11). The virtual-view contract spans chain links via the `agent_run_id` join.
428: 
429: 9. **TaskHeader status.** Mockup `r14-taskheader-chain-link-status.html`. Three variants:
430:    - Known estimate (after first handoff): `"link N of ~M, T hrs elapsed"`. `~M` is computed as `min(max_chain_length, max(N+2, ceil(estimated_total_steps / avg_steps_per_link)))` and refreshes per chain link.
431:    - Unknown estimate (before first handoff): `"link N of â€”"`. Tooltip explains "estimate available after the first chain handoff completes."
432:    - Terminal: `"{N} sessions, {H}h {M}m total"`.
433: 
434: 10. **Checkpoint-payload security.** Checkpoint payloads are sensitive task artefacts and MUST be:
435:     - **Encrypted at rest** where existing artefact infrastructure supports it. Concretely: the JSONB column is encrypted via the existing app-level encryption helper (the same helper used by `agent_run_payloads`'s redaction pipeline). If the helper is not yet wired for this column, the implementation chunk wires it.
436:     - **Scoped by org/subaccount/task.** The RLS policy on `operator_runs` enforces org+subaccount; the `task_id` (= `agent_run_id`) is implicit via the FK.
437:     - **Excluded from broad logs.** The adapter MUST NOT log `checkpoint_payload` contents at any log level. A grep gate (`scripts/gates/verify-no-checkpoint-logging.sh`) bans naive log calls referencing the column.
438:     - **Redacted in Run Trace by default.** The embedded screenshot is treated as an INTERNAL recovery artefact, not customer-visible. Customer-facing screenshots flow only through the harvested-artefact path (Â§ 3.12 / artefact harvester).
