 succeeded in 826ms:
1041: ## 7. Execution model
1042: 
1043: Per `docs/spec-authoring-checklist.md Â§ 5`, one model is picked explicitly and the rest of the spec is consistent with it.
1044: 
1045: ### 7.1 Adapter `dispatch()` â€” inline / synchronous (chain-link start)
1046: 
1047: The adapter's `dispatch()` call is **inline**: the caller (Spec A's dispatch orchestrator) waits for it to return. `dispatch()` does:
1048: 
1049: 1. Read `agent_runs` for `(organisation_id, subaccount_id)`.
1050: 2. Set the GUC; resolve effective caps (`subaccountOperatorSettingsService.getEffectiveSettings(subaccountId)`).
1051: 3. Concurrency-cap check (FOR UPDATE on `operator_runs` filtered to running slots; transactional). If new task hitting cap â†’ throw `OPERATOR_SESSION_LIMIT_EXCEEDED` (NOT queued, per Â§ 3.17 item 5). If chain-continuation hitting cap â†’ return a structured response that the chain-resume dispatcher handles by re-queueing (FIFO).
1052: 4. Three-way subaccount match (Â§ 6.7).
1053: 5. Resolve credential via `credentialBrokerService.requestOperatorSessionCredential` (or `resolveFallback` if stickiness is set).
1054: 6. Resolve / create profile via `operatorTaskProfileService.ensureActiveProfile(taskId, attemptNumber)`.
1055: 7. Insert the `operator_runs` row (status `'pending'`).
1056: 8. Call `sandboxExecutionService.runTask(...)` to start the sandbox session, injecting the credential and mounting the profile.
1057: 9. Receive the vendor session id; UPDATE the `operator_runs` row (status `'running'`, `started_at`, `vendor_session_id`).
1058: 10. Return `BackendDispatchResult` with `backendTaskId = operatorRun.id`.
1059: 
1060: A failure at any step (3â€“10) writes the chain-link row with status `'failed'` (or aborts before insert), emits the `operator.chain_link_start_failed` incident per Â§ 3.17, and the chain-link dispatcher (Â§ 7.3) handles retry/backoff.
1061: 
1062: ### 7.2 Chain-link terminal event â€” queued (pg-boss)
1063: 
1064: When the sandbox session terminates (operator runtime emits a terminal step-state OR hard cap is reached OR cancel propagated OR runtime crashed), the adapter writes the chain-link row to its terminal status and enqueues `'operator-session-completed'` with payload `{ operatorRunId, agentRunId }`.
1065: 
1066: The handler `operatorSessionCompletedHandler.ts`:
1067: 
1068: 1. Reads the `operator_runs` row (and its `checkpoint_payload`).
1069: 2. Calls `finaliseAgentRunFromBackend({ backendId: 'operator_managed', backendTaskId: operatorRunId })`.
1070: 3. Inside `finalise()`: the adapter decides task-terminal vs paused-for-continuation (per Â§ 3.14 item 4).
1071: 4. If task-terminal: parent agent run rolls up; cost rows are written via `operatorCostWriter.writeRowsForChainLink(operatorRunId)`; profile is scheduled for GC.
1072: 5. If paused-for-continuation: parent agent run sets `status='paused_for_chain_continuation'`; cost rows for THIS chain link are written via the same writer (per-chain-link cost rows happen regardless of pause/terminal); the chain-resume dispatcher enqueues `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` with payload `{ agentRunId }`.
1073: 
1074: **Idempotency posture (per Â§ 10.1):** key-based on `(operator_run_id, status)`. A re-delivery of the queue message is a no-op â€” the finaliser sees the row already in terminal state and returns the prior result.
1075: 
1076: ### 7.3 Chain-link dispatch â€” queued (pg-boss) with backoff retry
1077: 
1078: `operatorSessionDispatchNextChainLinkHandler.ts`:
1079: 
1080: 1. Reads the parent `agent_runs` row.
1081: 2. If status is not `'paused_for_chain_continuation'` (or `'delegated'` on the first dispatch â€” bootstrap path), no-op.
1082: 3. Calls `executionBackendRegistry.get('operator_managed').dispatch({ agentRunId, ... })` â€” re-uses Â§ 7.1 inline path.
1083: 4. On success: writes `agent_runs.status='delegated'`.
1084: 5. On failure with `'transient'` failure class: increments a retry counter on the agent run (`operator_chain_failure_count`), enqueues a delayed re-dispatch (1 min â†’ 5 min â†’ 15 min via pg-boss's `startAfter` parameter).
1085: 6. On the 3rd consecutive failure: writes `agent_runs.status='paused_chain_failure'`, emits `'operator-session.task_paused_chain_failure'` event, sends user notification.
1086: 7. On failure with `'permanent' | 'auth' | 'profile_corruption'` failure class: bypasses the backoff and goes directly to `paused_chain_failure`.
1087: 8. Every failure (transient or permanent) emits an `operator.chain_link_start_failed` incident with `retry_attempt` and `is_terminal`.
1088: 
1089: **Idempotency posture:** key-based on `(agentRunId, chain_seq_next)`. The chain_seq_next is computed from `max(chain_seq) + 1` for the task. Re-delivery of the queue message is a no-op when the chain link is already in `pending`/`running`/terminal state at that seq.
1090: 
1091: ### 7.4 Progress events â€” queued (pg-boss) + WebSocket bridge
1092: 
1093: Step-boundary events from the operator runtime are enqueued (`'operator-session-progressed'`) to keep the runtime's hot path off the DB. `operatorSessionProgressedHandler.ts`:
1094: 
1095: 1. Bumps `operator_runs.last_progress_at = now()` + `step_count += 1`.
1096: 2. Emits `'operator-session.progressed'` to the `agent-run:{runId}` WebSocket room via `emitAgentRunUpdate`.
1097: 
1098: The WebSocket bridge is best-effort: a dropped event is acceptable (the next event picks up the state). The polling fallback route is the durable visibility path.
1099: 
1100: ### 7.5 Profile GC â€” queued (pg-boss cron)
1101: 
1102: `operatorTaskProfileGcHandler.ts` is a 15-minute cron job that scans for `(status='scheduled_gc' AND scheduled_gc_at <= now())` rows, marks them `'gc_in_progress'`, deletes the underlying sandbox volume via the sandbox provider, then sets `'gc_done'`. Runs under `withAdminConnection` (cron-job principal) â€” does not require a tenant GUC because the scan is system-wide.
1103: 
1104: **Idempotency:** key-based on `(profile_id, scheduled_gc_at)`. A re-run of the cron during deletion picks up only rows still in `'scheduled_gc'`; rows transitioned to `'gc_in_progress'` are skipped.
1105: 
1106: ### 7.6 Cost-writer â€” inline within finaliser transaction
1107: 
1108: The cost-writer is **NOT a separate queue**. It runs inline within the `finalise()` transaction triggered by `'operator-session-completed'`. This is intentional: the cost rows must commit atomically with the chain-link terminal status to avoid the "terminal-but-no-cost" or "cost-but-not-terminal" partial state.
1109: 
1110: If the cost-writer fails: the entire `finalise()` transaction rolls back, the chain-link row stays in its prior state, and the pg-boss queue retries delivery. The cost-writer's own idempotency (key-based on `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)`) ensures the retry doesn't double-write.
1111: 
1112: ### 7.7 No new feature flags
1113: 
1114: Per framing (`spec-context.md`): `feature_flags: only_for_behaviour_modes`. The adapter registers unconditionally at boot. No `ENABLE_OPERATOR_BACKEND` flag. If the operator-session credential is unavailable for any subaccount, the existing connection-status surfaces the state.
1115: 
1116: ## 8. Phase plan
1117: 
1118: Single phase. **Phase 1** ships the whole Operator Backend end-to-end as defined here. The brief's D8 (chain-resume required, not a phase-3.5 deferral) and D11 (persistent profile required, not deferred) are honoured: no sub-phase splits the model.
1119: 
1120: The implementation chunks in Â§ 14 are sequential within Phase 1 but they are NOT phases â€” they are build-order ordering only. Each chunk leaves the system in a forward-compatible state (e.g. schema changes ship before the writers that depend on them).
1121: 
1122: **Out-of-phase deferrals** (Phase 3.5 / Phase 5) are listed in Â§ 11.

1125: 
1126: There is one phase, so phase-level sequencing is trivially satisfied. The chunk-level dependency graph in Â§ 14 has been checked against the three failure modes from `docs/spec-authoring-checklist.md Â§ 6`:
1127: 
1128: 1. **No backward dependency.** Every column referenced by code in Chunk N is created in an equal-or-earlier chunk's migration. Verified via the dependency table in Â§ 14.
1129: 2. **No orphaned deferrals.** Every "deferred" item is listed in Â§ 11. Cross-checked.
1130: 3. **No phase-boundary contradiction.** Only one phase; no boundary.

1134: ## 10. Execution-safety contracts
1135: 
1136: ### 10.1 Idempotency posture (per write path)
1137: 
1138: | Write path | Posture | Key |
1139: |---|---|---|
1140: | `operator_runs` insert (chain-link start) | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `INSERT ... WHERE NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM operator_runs WHERE agent_run_id=$1 AND chain_seq=$2)`. 0 rows-affected = a concurrent dispatcher already started this chain link. |
1141: | `operator_runs` terminal UPDATE | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status IN ('pending','running')`. 0 rows-affected = already terminal. |
1142: | `agent_runs` terminal UPDATE (task-terminal) | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status IN ('delegated','paused_*')` (the closed set of pre-terminal states). 0 rows-affected = already terminal; finaliser logs and returns 200 idempotent-hit. |
1143: | `agent_runs` pause UPDATE (`paused_for_chain_continuation`) | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status='delegated'`. 0 rows-affected = a concurrent path already paused or terminated. |
1144: | `operator_task_profiles` insert (first chain link) | **key-based** | unique constraint: `(task_id, attempt_number)`. 23505 â†’ catch and return the existing row (idempotent-hit). |
1145: | `subaccount_operator_settings` UPSERT | **key-based** | PK: `subaccount_id`. Conflict â†’ If-Match check (state-based concurrency control on top of key-based identity). |
1146: | `llm_requests` cost rows | **key-based** | unique index: `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)` for the new rows; existing `(agent_run_id, request_id)` for `per_token` rows. 23505 â†’ idempotent-hit. |
1147: | pg-boss `'operator-session-completed'` enqueue | **key-based** | pg-boss singleton key: `'operator-session-completed:' || operator_run_id`. Re-enqueue is a no-op. |
1148: | pg-boss `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` enqueue | **key-based** | singleton key: `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link:' || agent_run_id || ':' || chain_seq_next`. |
1149: | pg-boss `'operator-task-profile-gc'` cron tick | **state-based** | the cron handler's `UPDATE WHERE status='scheduled_gc' AND scheduled_gc_at <= now() RETURNING id` is the eligibility predicate; concurrent ticks see disjoint row sets. |
1150: | Audit-event write | **non-idempotent (intentional)** | every action records its own audit row; replays are intentional duplicates so the audit log captures every attempted-action. |
1151: 
1152: ### 10.2 Retry classification
1153: 
1154: | Operation | Classification | Notes |
1155: |---|---|---|
1156: | `credentialBrokerService.requestOperatorSessionCredential` | **guarded** | broker enforces its own idempotency; safe to retry on network errors. |
1157: | `sandboxExecutionService.runTask` | **unsafe** | a retry could spawn a duplicate sandbox. Wrapped by the `operator_runs` state-based idempotency boundary (above). |
1158: | `operatorCostWriter.writeRowsForChainLink` | **safe** | key-based idempotent. Retry is a no-op. |
1159: | `recordIncident` | **safe** | Spec C / existing pattern â€” incident ingestor is internally idempotent. |
1160: | WebSocket emission `emitAgentRunUpdate` | **safe** | best-effort; loss is acceptable. |
1161: | `operatorSessionDispatchNextChainLinkHandler` | **guarded** | wrapped by `operator_runs` (chain_seq) idempotency. |
1162: | `operatorTaskProfileGcHandler` | **guarded** | row-state predicate prevents double-delete. |
1163: | Profile-volume `delete` (Spec B provider call) | **unsafe** | a retry against a missing volume must be treated as success (the provider returns 404 â†’ treat as `gc_done`). Wrapped by `operator_task_profiles.status` predicate. |
1164: 
1165: ### 10.3 Concurrency guards
1166: 
1167: | Race | Guard |
1168: |---|---|
1169: | Two concurrent chain-link dispatchers for the same task | `operator_runs (agent_run_id, chain_seq)` UNIQUE + `INSERT ... WHERE NOT EXISTS`. First wins; second gets 0 rows-affected and re-queries to see the winner's row, then no-ops. |
1170: | Two concurrent task-cancel callers | `agent_runs` UPDATE with optimistic predicate on the pre-terminal closed set. First wins; second gets 0 rows-affected and returns 409 with the current state. |
1171: | Two concurrent dispatches racing past the concurrency cap | `SELECT count(*) FROM operator_runs WHERE subaccount_id=$1 AND status='running' AND superseded_by_attempt IS NULL FOR UPDATE` inside the dispatch tx. The `FOR UPDATE` serialises slot accounting. |
1172: | Two concurrent settings-PATCH calls | optimistic concurrency on `updated_at`. Second caller's `If-Match` mismatches â†’ 409. |
1173: | Two concurrent finalises for the same chain link | the finaliser's `operator_runs` UPDATE optimistic predicate gives one winner. The cost-writer's key-based idempotency gives second a no-op. |
1174: | Cron GC + admin debug-retention | the GC scan reads `scheduled_gc_at`; if an admin extends retention between scan and update, the row's `scheduled_gc_at` moves forward AND the cron's UPDATE-WHERE predicate (`status='scheduled_gc' AND scheduled_gc_at <= now()`) returns 0 rows on the second pass. Safe. |
1175: | Fresh-profile-restart racing in-flight chain link | the restart route requires the current chain link to be `'failed'` or the task to be `'paused_chain_failure'`. Optimistic predicate: `UPDATE agent_runs SET ... WHERE status IN ('failed','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded','paused_for_chain_continuation')`. A `running` chain link blocks restart. |
1176: 
1177: ### 10.4 Terminal event guarantees
1178: 
1179: **Chain-link terminal events** (one per chain link):
1180: 
1181: - Exactly one of `'operator-session.chain_link_completed' | '.chain_link_failed' | '.chain_link_cancelled'` per chain link.
1182: - Post-terminal prohibition: no further events with the same `chain_link_id` after a terminal event.
1183: - The terminal event's `status` is `'completed'` (with checkpoint OR final), `'failed'`, or `'cancelled'`. No `'partial'` at the chain-link level â€” partial completion of a chain link IS a `'completed'` with checkpoint (which is the normal case for non-final links).
1184: 
1185: **Task terminal events** (one per task, only on true terminal states):
1186: 
1187: - Exactly one of `'operator-session.task_completed' | '.task_failed' | '.task_cancelled'` per task.
1188: - Post-terminal prohibition: no further events with the same `agent_run_id` after a terminal event.
1189: - Paused states emit `'operator-session.task_paused_*'` events; they are NOT terminal â€” multiple may fire over a task's life (pause â†’ resume â†’ pause â†’ resume â†’ terminal).
1190: 
1191: ### 10.5 No-silent-partial-success
1192: 
1193: Every flow that can partially complete emits an explicit status. Concretely:
1194: 
1195: - A chain link that started but didn't finish a task â†’ `'chain_link_completed'` with checkpoint (NOT silent partial).
1196: - A task that hit the budget cap mid-chain-link â†’ the chain link `'chain_link_completed'` with checkpoint; the task `'task_paused_budget_exceeded'` (NOT a silent partial on the task).
1197: - A task that exhausted max chain length â†’ `'task_failed'` with `failure_reason='max_chain_length_reached'` (NOT silent).
1198: - A fallback-engaged chain link â†’ mixed cost rows per Â§ 3.12; both row types reflect the boundary explicitly.
1199: 
1200: ### 10.6 Unique-constraint â†’ HTTP status mapping
1201: 
1202: | Constraint | Violated when | HTTP status |
1203: |---|---|---|
1204: | `operator_runs (agent_run_id, chain_seq) UNIQUE` | Concurrent dispatch race | (internal â€” converted by `INSERT ... WHERE NOT EXISTS` to 0-rows; no HTTP exposure) |
1205: | `operator_task_profiles (task_id, attempt_number) UNIQUE` | Concurrent ensure-profile | 23505 caught, idempotent-hit, returns existing row body to caller. (Internal route's HTTP equivalent: 200 idempotent.) |
1206: | `subaccount_operator_settings (subaccount_id) PK` | UPSERT conflict | normal UPSERT semantics (no HTTP exposure). |
1207: | `llm_requests (operator_run_id, source_type, boundary) UNIQUE` (new) | Cost-writer retry | 23505 caught, idempotent-hit, returns 200. |
1208: | `subaccount_operator_settings` If-Match mismatch | Stale write | 409 `OPERATOR_SETTINGS_CONFLICT` with `current_state` in body. |
1209: | Cancel a task already in terminal state | optimistic predicate 0 rows | 409 `TASK_ALREADY_TERMINAL` with `current_status` in body. |
1210: | Fresh-profile-restart on running chain link | optimistic predicate 0 rows | 409 `OPERATOR_TASK_RESTART_BLOCKED` with `current_status` and `active_chain_link_id` in body. |
1211: | New operator task over concurrency cap | computed at dispatch | 429 `OPERATOR_SESSION_LIMIT_EXCEEDED` with `cap`, `current`, `subaccount_id` in body. |
1212: 
1213: No `23505` is allowed to bubble as a 500. The implementation chunk maps each via a typed exception class (`OperatorBackendConflictError`) â†’ mapper middleware that produces the 4xx response.
1214: 
1215: ### 10.7 State machine closures (`operator_runs`, `agent_runs`)
1216: 
1217: **`operator_runs.status` enum is CLOSED.** Adding a new value requires a spec amendment.
1218: 
1219: Valid transitions:
1220: 
1221: ```
1222: pending â†’ running          (sandbox session created, vendor_session_id populated)
1223: pending â†’ failed           (dispatch failure â€” auth, profile, runtime unavailable)
1224: pending â†’ cancelled        (user cancelled before sandbox started)
1225: running â†’ completed        (operator runtime terminal-success OR checkpoint-ready)
1226: running â†’ failed           (operator runtime crash OR heartbeat stale OR auth lost without fallback OR hard-cap unresumable)
1227: running â†’ cancelled        (user cancelled mid-link OR task-level cancel propagated)
1228: ```
1229: 
1230: Forbidden:
1231: - Any transition from `completed | failed | cancelled` (terminal).
1232: - `pending â†’ completed` (a chain link MUST be `running` before it can complete â€” there is no "skip the runtime" path).
1233: - `pending â†’ cancelled` from heartbeat-stale (cannot have a stale heartbeat without a running sandbox).
1234: 
1235: **`agent_runs.status` enum is CLOSED** (the Operator-Backend-relevant subset; the full enum is broader and pre-existing).
1236: 
1237: Valid transitions (operator-managed paths only):
1238: 
1239: ```
1240: pending â†’ delegated                                  (first chain dispatch)
1241: delegated â†’ paused_for_chain_continuation            (chain link completed with checkpoint, task not done)
1242: paused_for_chain_continuation â†’ delegated            (next chain link dispatched)
1243: delegated â†’ paused_chain_failure                     (3 consecutive dispatch failures)
1244: paused_chain_failure â†’ delegated                     (user retried)
1245: delegated â†’ paused_budget_exceeded                   (budget cap hit)
1246: paused_budget_exceeded â†’ delegated                   (user extended budget)
1247: delegated â†’ completed                                (final chain link task_completed)
1248: delegated â†’ failed                                   (operator runtime hard error OR max chain length OR hard-cap unresumable on non-retry path)
1249: {pending | delegated | paused_*} â†’ cancelled         (user cancelled)
1250: ```
1251: 
1252: Forbidden:
1253: - Any transition from `completed | failed | cancelled` (terminal).
1254: - `pending â†’ completed | failed | cancelled` without going through `delegated` (operator-managed tasks must enter delegation first).
1255: - `paused_* â†’ completed | failed` without re-entering `delegated` (a paused task MUST resume to dispatch a chain link before it can produce a task-terminal status).
1256: 
1257: Enforcement: optimistic predicates on every writer (Â§ 10.1, Â§ 10.3). No DB-level CHECK on transition graph (Postgres doesn't support state-machine constraints declaratively); the writer-level predicates are the enforcement.
1258: 
1259: **Adding a new status value:** any future spec adding to either enum MUST:
1260: 1. Add the value to the migration AND the union/type-annotation in the schema file.
1261: 2. Update this spec's state-machine diagrams (or supersede this spec).
1262: 3. Update every writer's optimistic predicates.
1263: 4. Update the UI status-pill renderer.
1264:

280: 5. **Cost-ledger semantics on mid-run swap.** The same chain link may produce **two** cost rows of the `credential_mode` boundary type: one `subscription_mediated` row for the pre-swap turns (`step_count` = turns up to swap) and one `per_token` row via the normal `llm_requests` path for the post-swap turns. Spec § 3.12 enumerates the attribution rules in full.
282: 6. **Fallback stickiness across chain links.** Once fallback engages in chain link N, it is **sticky for the logical task**: chain link N+1 starts with `credential_mode = 'api_key'`, NOT a re-attempt of the operator-session credential. Stickiness clears when:
283:    - The broker emits `operator-session.usability_restored` (Spec C reserved this signal; the broker side is wired in this spec).
285:    Absent either signal, fallback persists for the remainder of the task. Run Trace renders the `fallback_engaged` event once at the chain-link boundary where it first applied; subsequent chain links inheriting fallback show a passive `credential_mode: api_key` indicator without re-emitting the lifecycle event.
312: 2. **Per-step-boundary check.** Adapter sets a cancel flag on the chain-link row; the operator runtime checks the flag at each step boundary and exits cleanly.
328: The adapter MUST emit Run Trace events for: session start, credential injected (auth-type redacted), each step boundary, fallback engaged (if any), chain-link terminal status, artefact harvest, task-terminal status (final chain link only).
367: When fallback engages mid-chain-link: turns BEFORE the swap → counted in the chain link's `subscription_mediated` row (with `step_count` reflecting only the pre-swap turns); turns AFTER the swap → flow through the normal `llm_requests` writer with `source_type: 'per_token'`. The boundary is recorded in the `operator-session.fallback_engaged` event payload.
373: **Idempotency posture (per § 10.1):** all three writers are **key-based idempotent** on `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)`. A retry after partial commit MUST NOT double-write. The cost-writer is invoked exactly once per chain-link terminal event via the finaliser hook (Spec A pattern), not from the adapter's hot path. Boundary key for `subscription_mediated` is `(operator_run_id, 'subscription_mediated', 'chain_link')`. For `sandbox_compute`: `(operator_run_id, 'sandbox_compute', 'chain_link')`. For `per_token` rows that share a chain link with `subscription_mediated`: the existing `llm_requests` writer already keys on `(agent_run_id, request_id)`; this spec adds `operator_run_id` as a column on `llm_requests` (migration extends the existing schema).
420: 6. **Conversation history accumulation.** Per-chain-link blobs joined at read time, capped at last N chain links of context for the operator-model invocation. Concretely: each chain link writes a single artefact `operator-conversation-link-{operator_run_id}.json` to the existing artefact store. The resume payload composer reads the latest K (default 5) artefacts and concatenates them in chain order. K is a constant in `operatorConversationHistoryPure.ts`; not configurable per-subaccount in V1.
425:    - The state-machine boundary is at `pending → running`. The transition timestamp is `operator_runs.started_at` (set by the adapter immediately after the sandbox session is created and the credential is injected).
472: 4. **Profile lifecycle + retention.** Volume is created on first chain-link start (`status='active'`). Persists across chain links. After task-terminal: `status='scheduled_gc', scheduled_gc_at = now() + INTERVAL '48 hours'` (default). An admin (`org_admin`) may set `debug_retention_extended_by/_at` at task-terminal time, which extends `scheduled_gc_at` to `now() + INTERVAL '14 days'` for that task. Customer-visible artefacts (per § 3.12) are harvested into the artefact store BEFORE the volume is GC'd, regardless of retention window. A pg-boss cron job (`operator-task-profile-gc`, every 15 minutes) marks profiles `status='gc_in_progress'` when `now() >= scheduled_gc_at`, performs the volume delete via the sandbox provider, then sets `status='gc_done'`. Hard max lifetime including retention = `max_wall_clock_per_task_days` + 14 days.
481:    - **Conversation history resets at the attempt boundary.** Chain link 1 of attempt N+1 starts with the ORIGINAL task brief only.
483:    - **Old profile retained per § 3.15 item 4 retention rules** (default 48 hr after the attempt-superseded event; admin debug-retention extends to 14 days). The new attempt's volume is created fresh.

codex
1. **Section reference:** § 3.15 item 7 / § 3.3 indexes  
   **Issue:** Fresh-profile restart says attempt N+1 starts at chain link 1 with the same `agent_run_id`, but `operator_runs` has `UNIQUE (agent_run_id, chain_seq)`, which prevents chain_seq `1` from being reused across attempts.  
   **Suggested fix:** Change the index language to: “`(agent_run_id, attempt_number, chain_seq) UNIQUE — at most one chain link per task attempt sequence; `chain_seq` restarts at 1 for each `attempt_number`.”  
   **Severity:** critical

2. **Section reference:** § 3.16 “Settings application” / § 4.11  
   **Issue:** The spec says in-flight cap snapshots are pinned in the chain-link row, but `operator_runs` has no `settings_snapshot` column and `checkpoint_payload` does not contain `settings_snapshot`.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add to `operator_runs`: “`settings_snapshot jsonb NOT NULL` — effective `subaccount_operator_settings` values captured at dispatch time; all in-flight cap enforcement reads this snapshot, not the current settings row.”  
   **Severity:** critical

3. **Section reference:** § 7.3 item 5  
   **Issue:** The dispatch retry counter `operator_chain_failure_count` is load-bearing but no column, table, or reset writer is specified.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add either a column or explicit derived rule, e.g. “Add `operator_chain_failure_count integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` to `agent_runs`; increment only under `WHERE status IN ('delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation')`, reset to 0 on successful chain-link dispatch and user retry.”  
   **Severity:** critical

4. **Section reference:** § 3.10 item 2  
   **Issue:** Cancellation depends on “a cancel flag on the chain-link row,” but `operator_runs` has no cancel-request column.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add to `operator_runs`: “`cancel_requested_at timestamptz NULL`, `cancel_requested_by_user_id uuid NULL REFERENCES users(id)`; runtime step-boundary checks read `cancel_requested_at IS NOT NULL`.”  
   **Severity:** important

5. **Section reference:** § 7.2 / § 7.6  
   **Issue:** § 7.2 says the adapter writes the chain-link terminal status before enqueueing finalisation, while § 7.6 says terminal status and cost rows commit atomically inside the finaliser transaction.  
   **Suggested fix:** Replace § 7.2 with: “When the sandbox session terminates, the adapter records terminal observations in a non-terminal staging payload and enqueues `operator-session-completed`; the finaliser transaction is the only writer that sets `operator_runs.status` to `completed|failed|cancelled` and writes cost rows.”  
   **Severity:** critical

6. **Section reference:** § 3.9 / § 7.4  
   **Issue:** Progress handling is described twice with different writers: § 3.9 says the adapter increments `step_count`, while § 7.4 says the queued handler increments it, which can double-count or race on retries.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add: “Only `operatorSessionProgressedHandler.ts` mutates `last_progress_at` and `step_count`; the adapter only enqueues the event with a stable `(operator_run_id, step_index)` idempotency key, and handler retries use `step_count = greatest(step_count, step_index)`.”  
   **Severity:** critical

7. **Section reference:** § 10.1  
   **Issue:** `operator-session-progressed` is an externally triggered write path but has no idempotency posture in the § 10.1 table.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add a row: “`operator_runs` progress UPDATE | key-based | unique/event key `(operator_run_id, step_index)`; duplicate progress events are no-ops and never increment `step_count` twice.”  
   **Severity:** important

8. **Section reference:** § 3.17 item 5 / § 10.3  
   **Issue:** `SELECT count(*) ... FOR UPDATE` is not a sufficient concurrency guard for session slots; aggregate counts do not lock the absence of rows, so two dispatchers can both see capacity and start.  
   **Suggested fix:** Replace with: “Concurrency-cap checks acquire `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))`, then count running rows and insert/update the chain link in the same transaction.”  
   **Severity:** critical

9. **Section reference:** § 4.10 / § 5.2 / § 5.3  
   **Issue:** Cost idempotency requires `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)`, but the migration inventory only adds `operator_run_id` and an index, with no `boundary` column or unique constraint.  
   **Suggested fix:** Change migration `0331` to: “Add nullable `operator_run_id`, nullable `boundary text`, and `UNIQUE (operator_run_id, source_type, boundary) WHERE operator_run_id IS NOT NULL AND boundary IS NOT NULL`.”  
   **Severity:** critical

10. **Section reference:** § 4.10  
   **Issue:** The example ledger rows add fields such as `chain_seq`, `vendor_session_id`, `credential_mode`, `plan_tier`, `vcpu_seconds`, `wall_clock_ms`, and `peak_memory_bytes`, but no schema migration or metadata column mapping is specified for them.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add: “These operator-specific cost fields are stored in existing `llm_requests.metadata jsonb`; no new typed columns are added except `operator_run_id` and `boundary`.” Or enumerate every new column in migration `0331`.  
   **Severity:** critical

11. **Section reference:** § 3.17 item 4  
   **Issue:** Budget accounting refers to `sandbox_started_at` / `sandbox_completed_at`, but the locked `operator_runs` schema only has `started_at` / `completed_at`.  
   **Suggested fix:** Replace the language with: “Minutes consumed are measured using `operator_runs.started_at` and `operator_runs.completed_at`, written from DB `now()` inside the chain-link transaction.”  
   **Severity:** important

12. **Section reference:** § 3.14 items 3, 4, and 7 / § 10.7  
   **Issue:** Hard-cap unresumable is variously treated as `paused_chain_failure`, as a runtime failure that terminates the task, and as `delegated → failed` in the state machine.  
   **Suggested fix:** Pick one rule and state it everywhere, e.g. “`hard_cap_unresumable` always writes `operator_runs.status='failed', failed_mid_step=true` and transitions `agent_runs.status='paused_chain_failure'`; it is not task-terminal unless the user cancels or a later retry fails permanently.”  
   **Severity:** critical

13. **Section reference:** § 3.17 item 4 / § 3.14 item 4  
   **Issue:** Budget-cap auto-pause is specified, but the finaliser decision table has no branch for “completed with checkpoint because budget cap was reached,” so it would enqueue the next chain link.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add to § 3.14 item 4: “`completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` AND consumed budget >= pinned `per_task_budget_cap_minutes` → task pauses with `agent_runs.status='paused_budget_exceeded'`; do not enqueue the next chain link.”  
   **Severity:** critical

14. **Section reference:** § 3.7 item 6  
   **Issue:** Fallback stickiness across chain links has no source-of-truth storage or precedence rule, so implementers cannot know where to persist or clear it.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add a field such as: “`agent_runs.operator_credential_mode_override text NULL CHECK (...); 'api_key' means fallback is sticky for future chain links; NULL means resolve operator-session normally. `operator-session.usability_restored` and `refresh-credential` clear this field inside the resume transaction.”  
   **Severity:** important

15. **Section reference:** § 3.2 / § 4.1  
   **Issue:** The spec bans naked `'long_running'` literals while the adapter capabilities example uses string literals and only a type union is named as the canonical source, which provides no runtime value to import.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add: “`types.ts` exports `EXECUTION_CAPABILITIES = { LONG_RUNNING: 'long_running', ... } as const`; adapter objects and tests use `EXECUTION_CAPABILITIES.LONG_RUNNING` rather than string literals.”  
   **Severity:** important

16. **Section reference:** § 6.2 / § 7.5  
   **Issue:** `operator_task_profiles` has FORCE RLS, but the GC job is described as using `withAdminConnection` without a tenant GUC because the scan is system-wide; FORCE RLS can still block owner-bypass unless a bypass policy/principal is specified.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add: “The GC job runs as the existing maintenance role with `BYPASSRLS`; if that role is unavailable, the job must batch by `(organisation_id, subaccount_id)` and call `setOrgGUC()` before each scoped update.”  
   **Severity:** critical

17. **Section reference:** § 3.14 item 6 / § 5.1 / § 14 chunk 3  
   **Issue:** `operatorConversationHistoryPure.ts` is named as the home of a load-bearing constant, but it is absent from the file inventory and chunk plan.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add `server/services/operatorConversationHistoryPure.ts` to § 5.1 and Chunk 3 with purpose: “Pure helpers and constants for per-chain-link conversation-history windowing, including default `K = 5`.”  
   **Severity:** important

18. **Section reference:** § 3.13  
   **Issue:** The automatic CS notification `cs.operator_session.suspended_detected` is required, but no concrete producer file, handler, queue payload, or modified inbox pipeline file is named.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add a concrete file entry and contract: “`server/services/operatorSessionSuspensionNotifier.ts` exports `notifyOperatorSessionSuspended(input: OperatorSessionSuspensionNotificationInput): Promise<void>` and is called from fallback hard-fail and broker usability-state transitions.”  
   **Severity:** important

19. **Section reference:** § 6.2 / § 5.1  
   **Issue:** § 6.2 references a debug-retention-extend route, but § 5.1’s `server/routes/operatorTasks.ts` route list does not include it.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add to § 5.1: “`POST /api/operator-tasks/:agentRunId/extend-debug-retention` — org-admin route to extend profile retention to 14 days.”  
   **Severity:** minor

20. **Section reference:** § 10.3 / § 10.7 / § 3.15 item 7  
   **Issue:** Fresh-profile restart is allowed when `agent_runs.status='failed'`, but § 10.7 forbids any transition from terminal `failed`.  
   **Suggested fix:** Change the restart predicate to: “Fresh-profile restart is allowed only from `paused_chain_failure`, `paused_budget_exceeded`, or `paused_for_chain_continuation`; terminal `failed` is never restarted under the same `agent_run_id`.”  
   **Severity:** critical

21. **Section reference:** § 3.16 / § 3.17  
   **Issue:** `max_wall_clock_per_task_days` is a locked setting but no writer or scheduler path enforces it.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add: “At chain-link dispatch, if `now() - first_operator_run.started_at >= settings_snapshot.max_wall_clock_per_task_days`, do not dispatch; transition to `paused_budget_exceeded` with `failure_reason='max_wall_clock_exceeded'` or to a separately named paused state added to the enum.”  
   **Severity:** important

22. **Section reference:** § 3.11 / § 4.7  
   **Issue:** § 3.11 requires a Run Trace event for artefact harvest, but the closed lifecycle event set in § 4.7 has no artefact-harvest event.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add to § 4.7: “`operator-session.artefact_harvested` | After chain-link artefacts are harvested | `chain_link_id, artefact_ids, harvest_reason`.”  
   **Severity:** important

23. **Section reference:** § 3.1 / § 3.7  
   **Issue:** The adapter “does not branch on auth type at runtime,” but fallback, credential-mode persistence, and cost attribution all require branching on `operator_session` vs `api_key`.  
   **Suggested fix:** Replace with: “The adapter does not inspect provider-specific credential shapes; it does branch on the broker-returned redacted `mode` solely for credential injection, fallback stickiness, and cost attribution.”  
   **Severity:** important

24. **Section reference:** § 3.17 item 5 / § 7.3  
   **Issue:** Existing chain continuations over the concurrency cap are queued FIFO and “dispatched when a slot frees,” but no wake-up mechanism is specified when a running chain link completes.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add: “After every chain-link terminal finalise, `operatorChainSchedulerService.releaseSlotAndEnqueueNext(subaccountId)` scans the oldest queued continuation for that subaccount under the same advisory slot lock and enqueues exactly one eligible dispatch job.”  
   **Severity:** important

1. **Section reference:** § 3.15 item 7 / § 3.3 indexes  
   **Issue:** Fresh-profile restart says attempt N+1 starts at chain link 1 with the same `agent_run_id`, but `operator_runs` has `UNIQUE (agent_run_id, chain_seq)`, which prevents chain_seq `1` from being reused across attempts.  
   **Suggested fix:** Change the index language to: “`(agent_run_id, attempt_number, chain_seq) UNIQUE — at most one chain link per task attempt sequence; `chain_seq` restarts at 1 for each `attempt_number`.”  
   **Severity:** critical

2. **Section reference:** § 3.16 “Settings application” / § 4.11  
   **Issue:** The spec says in-flight cap snapshots are pinned in the chain-link row, but `operator_runs` has no `settings_snapshot` column and `checkpoint_payload` does not contain `settings_snapshot`.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add to `operator_runs`: “`settings_snapshot jsonb NOT NULL` — effective `subaccount_operator_settings` values captured at dispatch time; all in-flight cap enforcement reads this snapshot, not the current settings row.”  
   **Severity:** critical

3. **Section reference:** § 7.3 item 5  
   **Issue:** The dispatch retry counter `operator_chain_failure_count` is load-bearing but no column, table, or reset writer is specified.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add either a column or explicit derived rule, e.g. “Add `operator_chain_failure_count integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` to `agent_runs`; increment only under `WHERE status IN ('delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation')`, reset to 0 on successful chain-link dispatch and user retry.”  
   **Severity:** critical

4. **Section reference:** § 3.10 item 2  
   **Issue:** Cancellation depends on “a cancel flag on the chain-link row,” but `operator_runs` has no cancel-request column.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add to `operator_runs`: “`cancel_requested_at timestamptz NULL`, `cancel_requested_by_user_id uuid NULL REFERENCES users(id)`; runtime step-boundary checks read `cancel_requested_at IS NOT NULL`.”  
   **Severity:** important

5. **Section reference:** § 7.2 / § 7.6  
   **Issue:** § 7.2 says the adapter writes the chain-link terminal status before enqueueing finalisation, while § 7.6 says terminal status and cost rows commit atomically inside the finaliser transaction.  
   **Suggested fix:** Replace § 7.2 with: “When the sandbox session terminates, the adapter records terminal observations in a non-terminal staging payload and enqueues `operator-session-completed`; the finaliser transaction is the only writer that sets `operator_runs.status` to `completed|failed|cancelled` and writes cost rows.”  
   **Severity:** critical

6. **Section reference:** § 3.9 / § 7.4  
   **Issue:** Progress handling is described twice with different writers: § 3.9 says the adapter increments `step_count`, while § 7.4 says the queued handler increments it, which can double-count or race on retries.  
   **Suggested fix:** Add: “Only `operatorSessionProgressedHandler.ts` mutates `last_progress_at` and `step_count`; the adapter only enqueues the event with a stable `(operator_run_id, step_index)` idempotency key, and handler retries use `step_count = greatest(step_count, step_index)`.”  
   **Severity:** critical
